Discussion of Secondary Education

｜Resolutions｜

(1) Ratio of general, teacher training, commercial, and agricultural/industrial high schools.

(2) Private schools can receive subsidies after four years of registration.

(3) Other items passed except for the budget item which is reserved.

Wei Que said that the review report is generally very good, but it lacks guidance on vocational guidance and educational guidance, so the Secondary Education Group should pay attention.

Zhao Naichuan said that these two items should be supplemented.

▲Regulations for the Establishment of Secondary Schools

Zhuang Zexuan said that the restriction on general secondary schools is to seek vocational training for middle school students to facilitate their employment. This representative believes that the regulation that the general department and the agricultural and industrial departments each account for half of the total number of schools is not appropriate. "Item C, first item" should be changed to a ratio of one to three, that is, one general department and three agricultural and industrial departments. "Item C, second item" can remain unchanged.

Wang Maozu said that it is very difficult to run agricultural and industrial departments, and general departments should also be given attention. For example, Shaanxi Province has Northwest University but no high school, so it is difficult for students to get promoted. They must go to other provinces. After high school, they can take the university entrance exam. In Jiangsu, there are a total of twenty-one middle schools. If fourteen of them need to be converted into agricultural and industrial high schools, the equipment and other costs will be several million yuan. In reality, it may be very difficult.

Tang Shicheng said that the so-called general department in the plan includes commercial, teacher training, and clerical departments, so the ratio of each accounting for half is the ratio with the agricultural and industrial departments. Please pay attention to everyone. Moreover, the number of agricultural and industrial departments and general departments is half each, which already requires several schools to be converted in each province. Therefore, the number is already close to the general department.

Ou Yuanhuai said that the commercial department should not be included in the general department, but should also be regarded as a vocational department. Therefore, this representative believes that the high school general department and the high school agricultural, industrial, and commercial departments should account for a ratio of one to three.

Li Zhaochen seconded Ou Yuanhuai's proposal, with two reasons: (1) Universities have agricultural, industrial, and commercial colleges, and middle schools should also have agricultural, industrial, and commercial departments; (2) For the purpose of training staff for small shops, there should be middle school commercial departments.

Zhao Naichuan said that the inclusion of the commercial department in the general department is from the perspective of funding, because commercial department equipment is simpler than agricultural and industrial department equipment, and not from the perspective of vocational training, because agriculture and industry are vocational education and commerce is not.

Liu Zhan'en agreed to combine commerce and agriculture and industry into one category.

Chen Bulei said that the Secondary Education Group does not deny that the commercial department is vocational education. The reason for proposing the agricultural and industrial departments is nothing more than to increase national production during the period of political tutelage.

Zhu Jingnong said that agriculture, commerce, and industry should not be divided into large categories. The education of the Principle of People's Livelihood is vocationalized. Therefore, the separate listing of agriculture and industry is nothing more than from the perspective of funding.

Meng Xiancheng said that the items in this section can be changed to the ratio of senior high school general department, teacher training department, commercial department, domestic science department, and agricultural/industrial high schools. The majority passed the motion.

▲Rectify Private Middle Schools

Chen Dezheng proposed that item A of the third article of this section should be cancelled.

Zhao Naichuan said that the review group changed the period to seven years, which refers to newly established schools. The reason for setting it at seven years is to look at the performance of their graduates. Chen Dezheng said that junior high school graduation is only three years, so there is no need to set it at seven years. If the restrictions on private middle schools are too strict, it is tantamount to saying that public middle schools must be excellent and private middle schools must be bad. Therefore, it should be deleted to encourage those who are enthusiastic about running schools.

Zhao Naichuan said that the original plan was four years, but the review group changed it to seven years. Chen Dezheng proposed that the first item of the third section must be cancelled. Zheng Hongnian seconded the motion.

Zhu Jingnong said that this case can be voted on whether to delete it or not, and for seven years or four years. The chairman put it to a vote. The majority did not pass the deletion or seven years. As a result, the original plan was maintained that private middle schools can receive subsidies after four years.

▲Regulations for Connecting Middle Schools with Universities and Elementary Schools

Huang Jianzhong said that if all university facilities are based on high schools, there may be problems because the level of universities cannot be improved. Also, this section does not pay attention to vocational schools. Can it be deleted?

Zhao Naichuan said that the review committee will revise the text and distribute it to everyone, so there is no need to be confined to the wording.

▲Budget

Yu Qingtang said that except for the budget, the rest of this chapter can be passed. There was no objection from the public. The chairman then announced a ten-minute break.

Report from the Social Education Group

The meeting continued at 4:10 PM. Lei Peihong, chairman of the Social Education Group, reported the results of the review.

Summary of the Social Group's Review Results

(Detailed report, already recorded in yesterday's newspaper)

(1) In addition to the various articles stipulated in the principles of the implementation outline, it is proposed to specially use phonetic symbols as a medium for literacy within all activities in the scope of social education, so item G is added.

(2) It is proposed to industrialize the staff engaged in social education work, so the fifth article of the implementation outline has been revised.

(3) The main social education institutions sponsored by the central government are proposed to be prepared and established at the same time, but it is still proposed to set a time limit for their establishment separately, so the order and content stipulated in the original plan have been revised.

(4) It is proposed to popularize the social education industry sponsored by local governments, so the eighth and ninth items are added under the outline of "planning and promoting various main social education institutions".

(5) It is proposed to pay considerable attention to the education of the mentally and physically disabled, so some additions and changes have been made to "planning the establishment of special education and reformatory education methods".

(6) Civic training is an important task during the political period, and both school education and social education should share responsibility, so some additions and changes have been made to the cooperation methods between the two sides stipulated in the original plan.

Discussion of the Social Education Plan

｜Resolutions After Full Discussion by the Audience｜

(1) Each provincial education department and special city may establish social and mass education teacher training institutions.

(2) The preparatory office for the public theater should select foreign art talents familiar with foreign languages to study abroad.

(3) Other review reports passed except for the budget point which is reserved.

When discussing the improvement of the social education plan, Li Zheng proposed that if there is no objection to the review plan except for the budget point, it can be regarded as approved. Huang Shiheng said that the farmers' education center can be included in the mass education center, and there is no need to list the farmers' education center as a separate item. Chen Bulei said that some provinces have already established farmers' education centers, so there is no need to delete them. A bracket can be added to let each province do as they please. Huang Jianzhong said that in the fifth second line of the implementation outline, setting up social education departments in normal universities and various university education colleges is in accordance with the university regulations. As for the establishment of social education colleges or mass education colleges, there is no place for them in the university regulations, so there is no need to establish them separately. For the sake of cultivating talents, equivalent classes can be set up in universities or other schools in each province to proceed. Therefore, the first paragraph should be deleted. Sun Guiding agreed with Huang Jianzhong's proposal that there is no need to establish a separate social education college. It is only necessary to set up a social education department in the education college. Yu Qingtang said that in light of the situation of education in China, it is necessary to establish a social education college separately. Huang Jianzhong said that compulsory education and social education are equally important. Now the compulsory education college has been cancelled because it does not comply with the regulations, so there is no need to establish a social education college separately. Chen Dezheng said that it is better to change it to a social education training course or a mass education training course, which will not conflict with the university regulations and can take into account the fact that various provinces have already established this type of school. Chen Jianxiu said that the resolutions of this meeting do not have to adhere to the regulations, and for the sake of facts, each province has established them, so it is better to let each province do as they please. Tang Maoru said that the teachers of social education have a more complex target audience, including adults, youth, men, and women, etc., and are not compulsory education teachers, whose target audience is children, which is relatively simple. This must be paid attention to. As for the requirements of the facts, during the six-year period of political tutelage, the teachers must be trained by special organic institutions. This must be paid attention to. Therefore, he advocated retaining the original text of the review committee. Chen Dezheng said that a special city education bureau should be added under the education department of each province. Ou Yuanhuai said that the name should be changed to a social education or mass education teacher training institution for each province to choose from. Xie Shuying said that undertakings and knowledge develop from simple to complex. The basic department of the mass education college is the same as the education college, so there is no need to establish it separately and it should be cancelled. The chairman put it to a vote to change Ou Yuanhuai's proposal to each provincial education department and special city can establish a social education or mass education teacher training institution, and the majority passed the motion. Xie Shuying proposed that the preparatory office of the public theater should select graduates from specialist schools or above who are proficient in foreign languages and have artistic talents to go to various countries to study and conduct specialized research, and that except for the budget, it will be passed if there is no objection.

Ratio of Establishing General and Agricultural/Industrial Departments

▲Both Sides Debated for Half an Hour

▲The Result Still Maintains the Original Plan

At yesterday's General Assembly, regarding the item that the ratio of establishing high school general departments and agricultural/industrial departments should be based on the principle of each accounting for half, the members discussed for half an hour. Some advocated including commercial and domestic science departments in addition to agricultural and industrial departments, and some advocated maintaining the original plan of the review report. After a long discussion, it was voted on after twenty speeches.

The ratio of senior high school general teacher training commercial home affairs and other departments to the establishment ratio of agricultural and industrial departments should be based on the principle of each accounting for half.

Review of Education Fees

｜The Education Fees Group's Two Reviews Yesterday Resulted In｜

Maintaining the Independent Education Fees Case

Defining Central and Local Tax Revenues

From 9:00 AM on the 21st, the first education fees review meeting was held at the Ministry of Education Club. The committee members present were Wei Que, Huang Shiheng, Li Quanshi, Chen Dezheng, Hu Huahua, Zhang Honglie, Zheng Hongnian, Xu Shouzhi, Chen Bulei, Jiang Shaomo, Chen Hexian, Wei Tingsheng, and Wu Heling, totaling thirteen people. Zheng Yanghe was present as an observer. (1) Publicly elected Zheng Hongnian as chairman and Chen Dezheng as recorder. (2) Resolved to maintain the independent education funds case and drafted the detailed methods. Chen Bulei drafted these, and then it was submitted to a further review. (3) To divide central and local tax revenues and designate what kinds of tax revenue will be assigned for education fees, it was determined that Wei Tingsheng would be responsible for drafting. (4) Each group of proposed budget bills will be pushed through a modified version drafted by Chen Dezheng before it is submitted for a later review. (5) At 2:00 PM on the 21st, the second review meeting was still held at the Ministry of Education. (6) Wei Tingsheng discussed the contents of the draft plan for tax revenue division. Roughly: A. Full allocation to education fees includes wasteland. Fifty percent goes to the central government, thirty percent goes to the province, and twenty percent goes to the county and city. For wastelands of special counties, cities, and special municipalities, the central government and the city each get fifty percent. Estate tax, surcharges on tobacco and alcohol, and surcharges on land tax are all allocated at fifty percent to the central government, thirty percent to the province, and twenty percent to the county and city. The property of temples and monasteries should follow the usual practice and be credited to county and city revenues. B. Taxes and fees partly allocated to education expenses include Boxer indemnity, investment income, business tax, property tax, slaughter tax, etc.

Flexible Implementation of Plans Allowed

▲Zhang Honglie and Others Proposed Today

Member Zhang Honglie and others will propose to the General Assembly on the 22nd to add an article to the end of the resolutions of this meeting: "If special circumstances arise in a certain region during the implementation of this plan, the local provincial and municipal education administrative authorities may submit a plan to the Ministry of Education for flexible implementation." However, the majority of members believe that the plan resolved at this General Assembly has already paid special attention to local circumstances and has considerable flexibility. If another plan is stipulated, the implementation may be flexible at any time, and there are fears that the plan will be fundamentally shaken. Ouyang Yuanhuai and Others Propose a Resolution to Aid Education in Fujian

Members Ouyang Yuanhuai, Xu Shoushang, Wang Maozu, Tang Maoru, Zhuang Zexuan, Yu Qingtang, Jiang Li, Sun Zuosu, Chen Dezheng, Chen Heqin, Liu Zhanen, Wang Qiuhang, Jin Baoshan, Qiu Zhenzhong, Xu Jijie, Hou Hongjian, Zhuang Kuizhang, and others, proposed to the assembly a resolution to aid education in Fujian.

(Facts) According to the report by representatives Hou Hongjian and Zhuang Kuizhang, since Commissioner Cheng took office in Fujian's education department, he increased educational funding, reorganized primary and secondary schools, delineated public and private boundaries, and expanded educational endeavors. In over a year, the plans were being realized and were expected to yield results. However, the coup d'état on the 6th of this year led to Commissioner Cheng's arrest, initially detained in Yanping, and now in Youxi. His personal situation, mental state, and physical form are suffering. In the education department, not only are educational funds being withheld by various parties, preventing the implementation of various necessary measures, but also, due to the resulting influence, it is not uncommon to see education bureau chiefs and supervisors in various counties being beaten and expelled by local figures. School disturbances occur frequently, and the decline in academic atmosphere is beyond repair. With the provincial government in a state of anarchy, there is little hope for education. Although this National Education Conference is limited to discussing proposals, given the recent situation in Fujian as described above, what should our sentiments be? This report is a brief overview of the situation, and we must devise methods to aid the educational situation in Fujian.

(Reasons) Fujian is an important province in the South. According to the report, various chaotic states have plunged it into anarchy. The Education Commissioner has been unjustly arrested due to political changes. For three to four months, the central government has not resolved the issues in Fujian, and the Ministry of Education has not implemented any measures for the province's education. Although this conference has limitations on the scope of discussion, the colleagues believe it would be regrettable to ignore and not discuss such a significant matter concerning Fujian. We must devise methods to aid the situation. Therefore, a temporary motion is proposed to the assembly for discussion, petitioning the Ministry of Education to take action. Whether this is feasible should be decided by public vote.

Fujian People's Association for National Salvation Requests Assistance with Cheng's Case

The Fujian People's Association for National Salvation telegraphed the entire Education Conference on the 20th, stating that Lu Xingbang, the commander of the newly formed Second Division of Fujian, has detained Education Commissioner Cheng Shikui and others for over three months. They requested that a special case be submitted to the central government for handling.

Administrative Discussion Conference to be Held After the Closing of the General Assembly

▲ The 24th and 25th

▲ The conference is changed to a discussion

The Ministry of Education had originally planned to hold a National Education Administrative Conference after the closing of the General Education Conference. However, to avoid various disputes and discussions, the Ministry has decided to change the Administrative Conference into an Administrative Discussion Conference. The attendees are to be representatives from each province at the level of Education Commissioner or section chief and above, as well as the Education Bureau Chiefs of special municipalities. The conference is scheduled for the 24th and 25th. The cases that the Ministry of Education had planned to propose have now been canceled and replaced with a discussion format to exchange ideas.

▲ Review Report of the Overseas Chinese Education Group

This group held its first review meeting on the 16th of this month, from 2:00 PM to 5:00 PM. Those present were Zheng Hongnian, Ouyang Yuanhuai, Zhao Naichuan, Zhuang Zexuan, Zhu Baoqin, Qian He, and Liu Shimu. Those attending as observers were Wu Zhuoyin and Gao Xing. Zheng Hongnian was publicly elected as chairman, and Zhu Baoqin as secretary. The second review meeting was held from 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM on the morning of the 17th. Those present were Qian He, Zhao Naichuan, Zhuang Zexuan, Zhong Yingguang, Liu Shimu, Zhu Qinbao, and Zheng Hongnian. As a result of the three meetings, there was general agreement with this plan, with some additions, deletions, or modifications, which are listed below:

(1) For item A of the second section of "Organization," the text after "Before the establishment of the said department" is proposed to be amended as follows:

The Overseas Chinese Education Department should be established in the shortest possible time. Before the department is established, the Ministry of Education should appoint senior officials (the number to be determined by the Ministry) to handle Overseas Chinese educational administrative affairs and implement the various plans formulated by the Design Committee.

(2) It is proposed to add an item 5 after the fourth section of "Organization," with the original 5th and 6th sections becoming the 6th and 7th. The proposed added text is as follows:

5. The Ministry of Education should, in the shortest possible time, send inspectors to various regions to conduct on-site inspections of Overseas Chinese education. (These inspectors are different in nature from the commissioners mentioned in the third and fourth articles and should operate in parallel.)

A. The total amount is 10 million yuan.

2. 600,000 yuan from the Guangdong Provincial Government.

3. 400,000 yuan from the Fujian Provincial Government.

The above three items should be fully allocated in one go in the 19th year.

4. 7 million yuan to be raised from the Overseas Chinese community over six years.

(6) It is proposed to delete the seven words "prefixed with the words Overseas Chinese and" in item A of the first section of "School Education."

This group requests the Ministry of Education to pay attention to the following points when implementing this plan:

1. The Design Committee should formulate detailed implementation rules based on this plan.

2. The allocation of educational funds should be based on the opinion of the Overseas Chinese Education Association, and detailed measures should be formulated.

3. The Ministry of Education should pay special attention to the selection of candidates when selecting educational commissioners and inspectors.

4. The Overseas Chinese Education Association should be established as soon as possible, and a suitable location should be studied.

▲ Higher Education Group Review Meeting

The Higher Education Group held its fifth review meeting on the 22nd. The meeting began at 9:00 AM yesterday at the Ministry of Education. (2) Starting this year, funding for establishing national specialized schools should be increased. The first year will be 300,000 yuan, and then increased by 200,000 yuan each year until it reaches 1.5 million yuan. (3) Starting this year, the Central Government should increase annual funding by 300,000 yuan to subsidize private universities. (4) The Central Government should increase annual funding for studying abroad by 300,000 yuan to increase the number of students sent abroad. (5) The subsidy fund for academic research groups should be set at 6 million yuan, to be allocated over ten years starting this year.

Various Aspects of the General Assembly

▲ Jiangsu Education Department Sends Education Overview

▲ The content is divided into six parts...totaling hundreds of thousands of words

Jiangsu Education Commissioner Chen Hexian believes that this National Education Conference brings together education personnel from across the country, an opportunity not to be missed. To introduce the current state of education in Jiangsu Province, he specially instructed the department to compile and print a book titled "Recent Educational Overview of Jiangsu Province." The content is divided into six parts: educational administration, higher education, secondary education, elementary education, social education, and educational funding, totaling several hundred thousand words. A thick volume has been bound and was sent to the reception of the National Education Conference yesterday for distribution.

▲ Vocational Education Society Welcomes Attending Members

The China Vocational Education Society will welcome members from all provinces attending the National Education Conference in Shanghai. Yesterday, the society sent letters to its members, stating, "We respectfully acknowledge your hard work during these days of meetings. Our society has been established for thirteen years, and thanks to the support of various parties, it has some facilities. However, we believe that our colleagues bear heavy responsibilities, but their talents and abilities are limited, and all improvement matters still require guidance from those with expertise. We are delighted to hear that you are coming to the capital and are eager to seek advice from experts, but we are afraid of disturbing you due to the importance of the conference affairs. We plan to welcome you in Shanghai after the closing of the General Assembly to respectfully listen to your instructions. Here is a copy of the China Vocational Education Society in the Republic of China, year 18, for your review, and we hope you will kindly point out any errors."

The Jiangsu Provincial People's Education Hall will hold an expanded propaganda week for people's education in Zhenjiang County Hall from the 22nd to the 28th, divided into display and propaganda. The exhibits related to people's education, such as books, forms, and tools, are very rich. In addition to inviting people to give speeches, there will also be performances by artists in the evening. It is reported that the colleagues preparing the People's Education Propaganda Week are wholeheartedly welcoming all members of the National Education Conference to visit and provide guidance.

Plans for the Establishment of National Vocational Schools by Huang Jianzhong

In the Higher Education Group's plan, many proposals were entirely removed during the final compilation, including the plan to establish national vocational schools. (We have found the original text drafted by Huang Jianzhong and record it as follows for reference.)

Universities emphasize theory, while vocational schools emphasize application. Although this concept has been challenged in recent times, many countries, both Eastern and Western, still have vocational schools and universities existing side by side. Higher education in our country has traditionally been divided into universities and specialized schools. In the twelfth year of the Republic [1923], there were a total of 125 private specialized schools and universities nationwide, with universities accounting for 35 and specialized schools numbering 90. By the fourteenth year [1925], the number of specialized schools had decreased to 85 (according to statistics from the China Education Improvement Association over the years). In the fifteenth year [1926], the number further decreased to 62 (according to a survey of national specialized schools and above by the former Beijing Education Ministry). Currently, including newly established national vocational schools, there are only 50. Moreover, there are approximately 20 public and private law and medical specialized schools scheduled to close. Since the thirteenth year of the Republic [1924], many specialized schools have been transformed into universities, leading to a trend of neglect. The drawbacks of specialized schools in the past are also worth noting. During the late Qing dynasty's preparations for constitutionalism, provinces established numerous law and political science schools. This trend continued into the early Republic, resulting in a plethora of so-called specialized schools, particularly in law and political science, which were often poorly run. They relied solely on lecture notes, lacked libraries, and students could graduate without attending classes regularly. Although specialized schools in agriculture, industry, commerce, and medicine were comparatively better, their curricula were often superficial and lacked practical training. The short duration of medical schools was especially inappropriate. Recognizing the immense importance of law and medicine to social survival and national life, the Ministry of Education issued a clear order in July of the eighteenth year [1929], stipulating that public and private law and medical specialized schools could only continue until their existing students graduated and were prohibited from recruiting new students from the eighteenth academic year onward. Other provincial, public, and registered private vocational schools in agriculture, industry, commerce, fisheries, library science, etc., were instructed to change their names and organizations in accordance with the "Vocational School Organization Law and Regulations." At the same time, provincial and municipal governments were consulted to assess local conditions and determine the necessity of establishing additional vocational schools, and if so, which were most urgent. Except for the provinces of Jilin, Heilongjiang, and Xinjiang, which responded that there was no need to establish additional schools, and Shandong, Hebei, and Fujian, which had instructed their education departments to review the matter but had not yet provided a clear response, eighteen other locations had responded, suggesting the establishment of as many as thirty-five different types of vocational schools. Among them, vocational schools specializing in forestry, agronomy, leather manufacturing, fisheries, civil engineering, mechanical engineering, statistics, papermaking, mining and metallurgy, animal husbandry, sericulture, and shipbuilding were considered particularly urgent for establishment by various provinces and cities (Note 1). The requests from various organizations and legal entities to establish vocational schools were also numerous (Note 2).

Although higher education in Europe and America is mostly concentrated in universities, technical personnel are often trained in vocational schools. Educational systems vary from country to country. Some institutions resemble vocational schools but are actually universities. For example, the Colorado School of Mines in the United States prides itself on training fully qualified engineers. Its program lasts four years and confers degrees, making it essentially a university, equivalent to an independent college in our current system. In France, Switzerland, and Italy, there are many renowned vocational schools with a three-year program that emphasizes rigorous coursework. Graduates are employed by the state and society, and vocational school graduates are often more welcomed by society than university graduates. In Britain, higher education is largely dominated by famous universities, each comprising more than ten schools or colleges scattered throughout the country, granting both degrees and diplomas. University programs generally last three years, while specialized courses vary between one and two years. Therefore, the boundary between vocational schools and universities is difficult to define, and independent vocational schools are relatively few.

Our country has a vast territory, and the development of industry is urgently needed. However, the establishment of any large factory requires the planning of foreign engineers and the management of specialists. This incurs significant costs, and the equipment used often reflects the nationality of the hired engineers. Americans tend to favor American-made equipment, while the British favor British-made equipment, regardless of whether the equipment is the latest invention. The sole criterion for selection is the engineer's nationality. What our country urgently needs now is various types of personnel who can serve as foremen, technicians, and engineers. Vocational schools train foremen, universities train engineers, and vocational schools train technicians, who are intermediate between foremen and engineers. Graduates of vocational schools should start as foremen, gradually advance to technicians, and eventually become engineers. The state must first have a solid core of technical experts before it can talk about an industrial revolution.

Some argue that universities can establish specialized courses with the same entrance requirements and duration as vocational schools, making it unnecessary to re-establish vocational schools. However, vocational schools are limited to applied sciences and arts, unlike university specialized courses, which can involve social sciences. If a university is located in an area without a vocational school, it may establish specialized courses similar in nature to vocational schools. In areas without universities or where a university lacks a specific department, a specific type of vocational school should be established based on local needs. Moreover, vocational schools come in many types with small scope, limited funding needed based on local conditions, and the talent they cultivate will be ideally suited for material construction after the period of political tutelage. In addition to provinces and cities raising their own funds to establish provincial and municipal vocational schools, a plan to establish national vocational schools is outlined below.

First National Forestry Vocational School: Dr. Sun Yat-sen cared deeply about the people's livelihood and listed the construction of forests in northern and central China as a key objective in his industrial plan. In recent years, floods and droughts have been frequent, and food shortages have been prevalent. Afforestation can prevent disasters and increase food production. Therefore, the establishment of a national forestry vocational school is a matter of urgency. National vocational schools should focus on cultivating specialized afforestation personnel to be deployed throughout the country. The location of this school should be convenient. Lushan is located in central China with convenient transportation. Guling is a resort for Chinese and foreigners. Creating a model forest here would not only be visually impressive but also facilitate practical training. An Dong and Qingdao are also suitable locations. In the future, Liaoning Province should establish a provincial forestry vocational school, and Qingdao Municipality should establish a municipal forestry vocational school.

Second National Textile Vocational School: Regarding the silk industry, China produces approximately three million dan of silk annually, with Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces accounting for the majority. Of this, about nine-tenths of the silk produced in the Jiangnan region is woven into silk fabrics for domestic consumption, while one-tenth is our country's largest export commodity, with annual exports of around 100,000 dan (worth approximately 70 million taels), of which Shanghai accounts for three-fifths. Regarding the cotton industry, the lower reaches of the Yangtze River are the most productive cotton-growing region in our country. Nantong, Changshu, Taicang, Jiading, and Shanghai are all famous for producing cotton of the highest quality, suitable for spinning. Zhengzhou is also a cotton market center. In the eleventh year of the Republic [1922], there were 73 yarn mills nationwide, with Shanghai having the most at 28, employing 300,000 workers. Unfortunately, after the European War, both the silk and yarn industries have declined, unable to compete with foreign factories. One of the reasons for this failure is the lack of specialists. To utilize education to recover our rights and interests, it is proposed to establish a National Textile Vocational School in Wuxi or Zhengzhou, with special emphasis on the research of rayon. This would facilitate student practice and meet the needs of the local area (to be completed in the first year of the period of political tutelage).

Third National Paper-Making Vocational School: The fifth plan in Dr. Sun Yat-sen's industrial plan, specifically the section on the printing industry, states: "Currently, the paper used by Chinese newspapers is all imported from foreign countries. Paper is an important tool for disseminating culture. China has many raw materials for paper making, such as the natural forests in the northwest and the reeds near the Yangtze River, which can all be used as excellent paper materials." There was a former paper mill in Chenjiaji, Hubei. The National Paper-Making Vocational School should be established there.

Fourth National Mining and Metallurgy Vocational School: Mining and metallurgy are fundamental industries and the primary drivers of material civilization and economic progress. Our country is richest in mineral resources in the southwest, with Yunnan being particularly abundant in copper, iron, silver, and tin. A National Mining and Metallurgy Vocational School should be established in Kunming (to be completed in the second year of the period of political tutelage).

Fifth National Shipbuilding Vocational School: The third plan in Dr. Sun Yat-sen's industrial plan, specifically the section on establishing shipyards, states: "With China's cheap labor and abundant materials, construction should be cheaper than in foreign countries. Besides the naval fleet, we also need to build a large fleet of inland river shallow-water vessels and fishing boats. It is not easy to transport such small boats across the ocean on ships. Therefore, foreign shipyards cannot build these types of vessels for us. China must at this time have its own shipyards to build its own shallow-water vessels and fishing fleets." Shanghai is a major international trading port and the gateway to the Yangtze River. It already has shipyards available for student practice. Therefore, it is proposed to establish a National Shipbuilding Vocational School there.

Sixth National Aircraft Manufacturing Vocational School: French General Foch stated, "The world wars of the future will be decided in the air." Dr. Sun Yat-sen also issued a decree on national salvation through aviation, highlighting the importance of the aviation industry to national defense. In terms of transportation, airplanes have the same functions as trains and ships, but their speed is ten times faster. Facilitating communication and saving time are both important. Our country's aviation industry is just beginning to emerge, and the demand for airplanes will increase as it gradually expands. Therefore, it is proposed to establish an Aircraft Manufacturing Vocational School in Pukou, with an attached automobile manufacturing department (to be completed in the third year of the period of political tutelage).

Seventh National Reclamation and Colonization Vocational School: Colonizing Mongolia and Xinjiang is mentioned in the third section of the first plan in Dr. Sun Yat-sen's industrial plan: "If we can implement our colonization policy using scientific methods, the results will be unparalleled." The northwest frontier is desolate and in urgent need of development. High schools specializing in reclamation and colonization should be established locally as a pioneering effort for colonization. A National Reclamation and Colonization Vocational School would be most suitable for establishment in Dihua.

Eighth National Animal Husbandry Vocational School: The livestock produced in Mongolia, such as cattle, sheep, camels, and horses, are of excellent quality and in large quantities. A recent survey of the three provinces of Inner Mongolia, Rehe, Chahar, and Suiyuan shows that they produce 484,500 jin of camel wool, 260,100 jin of sheep wool, 27,020 cow hides, 10,910 horse hides, and 72,800 sheep skins. In addition, they also produce 60,000-70,000 jin of cashmere and over 100,000 jin of fox fur. All of these are raw materials for the wool textile and leather industries, and Suiyuan has plans to establish wool and leather factories. However, to develop the wool and leather industries, fundamental improvements in the animal husbandry industry are needed. If natural pastures can be utilized and scientific guidance can be provided, our country's animal husbandry industry can easily compete with the United States and Australia. Therefore, it is proposed to establish a National Animal Husbandry Vocational School in Suiyuan, with attached wool weaving and leather making classes (to be completed in the fourth year of the period of political tutelage).

Ninth National Fisheries Vocational School: Our country's territorial waters, in addition to producing shrimp, crabs, scallops, dried razor clams, shark fins, sea cucumbers, mussels, lizard skin, abalone, and various fish and turtles, also produce precious items such as conch shells and tortoiseshells. Unfortunately, ineffective fishing methods have allowed Japanese fishermen to dominate coastal fisheries. Our fishermen lack knowledge and are facing a dire situation. Dr. Sun Yat-sen's industrial plan calls for the establishment of 31 fishing ports along the Chinese coast, from Andong near the Korean border to Qinzhou near the Vietnamese border, averaging one port every 100 miles of coastline. This would complete China's fisheries plan. To revitalize fisheries education and cultivate fisheries talent, relying solely on existing fisheries vocational schools is insufficient. A National Fisheries Vocational School should be established in Qingdao (to be completed in the fifth year of the period of political tutelage).

Tenth National Industrial Vocational School: Material construction depends on machinery. A complete industrial vocational school must be established to manufacture machinery independently. Switzerland, with a small area and a population of only a few million, has a renowned complete industrial vocational school in Zurich. It is divided into eleven departments: architecture and civil engineering, mechanical engineering, electrical engineering, chemistry, pharmacy, forestry, agriculture and rural engineering, mathematics and science teacher training, natural sciences, and military science. There are also optional general courses: Category A includes literature, history, philosophy, economics; Category B includes mathematics, natural sciences, engineering, and military science. German, French, or Italian language classes are also offered. Our country should establish a similar complete industrial vocational school in Chongqing, although the departments need not be as extensive and complex (to be completed in the sixth year of the period of political tutelage).

My Hope for the Entire Church (Lu Shaoji)

The various educational plans discussed at this National Education Conference in our country are in accordance with the educational aims of the Republic of China, as resolved by the Third National Congress of the Chinese Kuomintang: "The education of the Republic of China, based on the Three Principles of the People, aims to enrich the people's lives, support social survival, develop the national economy, and perpetuate the nation's life, striving for national independence, universal civil rights, and economic development, to promote world harmony." - Dr. Sun Guiding.

We can say that this is similar to the aims of the "World Education Conference" initiated by the National Education Association of the United States in 1923. The aims of the World Education Conference are "to seek cooperation in international education, disseminate educational information from various countries, promote goodwill among nations, and enhance world peace," also seeking world harmony.

However, the purpose of my writing this article is not to compare this National Education Conference with the World Education Conference, but to express three hopes for this National Education Conference:

(1) Since the aims of this National Education Conference in our country are the same as those of the World Education Conference, this conference seems to have both internal and external aspects. It must not only find ways to improve Chinese education but also promote world education. Therefore, I hope that the education experts attending the conference will pay attention to the following points:

(1) How can we exchange educational books, newspapers, and dissertations with educational institutions and experts in various countries?

(2) How can we exchange teachers with various countries, and what should be the methods for subsidizing students studying abroad?

(3) Should we use school textbooks to disseminate the national conditions and ideals of various countries?

(4) Should we advocate the establishment of an "International Education Institute" to unite world education?

(5) Should we jointly organize a "World Goodwill Association" with various countries, dedicated to promoting friendly relations among nations?

Performance by the Southeast Women's Physical Education School

Photographed by Guanghua, Nanjing

(2) Our country was founded on the Three Principles of the People. Although we are now in the period of political tutelage, there are still few Westerners who sympathize with us. The reason for this is that our people have not worked hard to promote our ideas abroad, and all books about Party doctrines are in Chinese, which foreigners cannot read. Therefore, I cannot help but hope that our country's education authorities will quickly send several copies of the "English San Min Chu I" (San Min Chu I), published by the Commercial Press and translated by Mr. F.W. Price and Mr. He Bingsong, to foreign governments, educational institutions (such as educational administrative bodies and university libraries in various countries), and education experts, so that Westerners who do not know Chinese can also learn about the doctrines created by Dr. Sun Yat-sen and sympathize with us.

(3) Foreigners are currently isolated from news about our country (only knowing that we have military activities). Therefore, I hope that our country's education authorities will translate the resolutions of this National Education Conference into English or other languages and, in addition to sending several copies to educational institutions and experts in various countries, our representatives must bring them to the next World Education Conference and read them in the conference hall, hoping to popularize the education of the Three Principles of the People in the world and realize the advocacy of "World Harmony."

Leaders of the education community, will you consider my humble opinion as acceptable?

Fourth Day of the National Scout General Review

Yesterday, Paying Respects at the Mausoleum... Today, Closing Ceremony

▲ All Scouts Pay Respects at the Mausoleum

The Line Extended Over Four Li

Presided Over by Dai Jitao

At 7:00 AM, all scouts departed from the military officer training camp, and it took until 8:00 AM for the departure to be completed. They walked along Zhongshan Road, with the line extending over four li. By 10:30 AM, all had arrived at the mausoleum. The heads of each troop, staff members, and scout service personnel were arranged in twelve lines in the memorial hall. The scouts from each troop were arranged in front of the memorial platform to pay their respects. The ceremony was presided over by Dai Jitao, Minister of the Central Training Department, with Zhao Genyao as the master of ceremonies. The Liangjiang Girls' Scouts and the Poor Children's Home orchestra played music and sang the Party song. The presiding official presented a wreath, and all saluted Dr. Sun Yat-sen's portrait with the highest respect. The presiding official reverently read Dr. Sun Yat-sen's will, and all read it aloud in unison, followed by twenty-three minutes of silence. They sang the Scout song, and then Dai Jitao, Liu Luyin, Zhang Daofan, and Shi Weihuan, the director of the office, led all in viewing the remains. The viewing was completed around 1:00 PM. Finally, Dai Jitao summoned the service personnel from each troop in front of the tomb and delivered a very sincere speech.

▲ Commemoration Week Held

| Dai Jitao's Report |

Encouraging Aspiration to Build a Strong Nation

At 2:00 PM on the 20th, after paying respects at the mausoleum, the scouts gathered in front of the memorial platform to hold a commemoration week. Chairman Dai delivered a report, stating in essence: "Today, we have gathered scouts from all over the country to Dr. Sun Yat-sen's mausoleum. We all sincerely and unanimously commemorate Dr. Sun Yat-sen. You must know that our China, our Chinese nation, has been unfortunate for many years. In the past century, we have suffered great oppression and bullying from imperialists. It was Dr. Sun Yat-sen's revolution that overthrew the oppressive Manchu government and created the Republic of China, a national state for all Chinese people. Our country is still under construction. All social organization, training, and material construction must be created from now on, like steps, stepping up one by one to achieve excellence. To complete an excellent country, we need all the people to be united, and each generation must be stronger than the last. Only through continuous efforts over ten or a hundred years can we create a glorious and brilliant nation and an excellent national culture. This responsibility rests entirely on you, little sisters and brothers. Your new responsibility is very important. You must unite, train well in all aspects of spirit, physical strength, intelligence, and morality, so that when you go out into society, no matter what occupation you are in, whether agriculture, industry, or commerce, you will be leaders of those who have not had the opportunity to receive education, and only then can you achieve your goals. Today, as we commemorate Dr. Sun Yat-sen here, we must aspire to be a truly strong nation." After speaking, he led all in shouting slogans, took photos, and dispersed.

Establishment of the Chinese Textile Institute

▲ Aim: To Seek Progress in Technology and Management

The Chinese Textile Institute, organized by textile experts from across the country, held its inaugural meeting at No. 80 Avenue Édouard VII, Shanghai, on the afternoon of the 20th of this month, after three months of preparation. More than 120 members from Shanghai, Nantong, Haimen, Wuxi, Changzhou, Jiujiang, Hankou, and other places attended. The Municipal Training Association specially sent Mr. Xu Yefu to attend and provide guidance. Mr. Zhu Xianfang, the chairman, presided over the meeting, and after formal opening rites, the chairman delivered an opening speech, stating that China's modern textile industry has a history of 43 years. However, imports of foreign textile products continue to increase year by year, which is a deep shame for those of us engaged in the textile industry. The reason why China's textile industry lags behind to this extent is that technical personnel have never been united, and there have been few opportunities for research and discussion. Now, driven by our conscience, we have gathered loyal individuals to form this institute to seek progress in technology and management. We hope that all members will work together with one heart and one mind to plan progress, bearing obligations without rights, and that we can reap satisfactory results in the future. Next, Mr. Zhang Diesheng, a member of the preparatory committee, reported on the preparatory process. Afterwards, Mr. Xu Yefu, the representative of the Party Department, and Mr. Qian Yongli, the representative of the textile department of Nantong University, delivered speeches, mostly offering words of encouragement. At this point, the constitution was discussed and resolutions were made article by article, and a declaration was issued, stating the institute's mission. Subsequently, Zhu Xianfang, Zhu Gongquan, Wang Fuli, Zhang Diesheng, Huang Bingkui, Lu Shaoyun, Wu Xiangzhi, Huang Yunqiu, Su Jiquan, Gong Yinshan, Ren Liqing, Chen Zhongjie, Qian Changshi, Yang Yutian, and Si Zuozhou, fifteen people in total, were elected as executive committee members. Wang Zisu, Shen Yanmou, Chen Shouyi, Yuan Zhongqi, and Liu Daoqiu, five people, were elected as alternate committee members. The representative of the Party Department then administered the oath and announced their assumption of office. A group photo was taken and a meal was held in commemoration. This was truly the first grand gathering of textile experts from across the country.

Sports

The Situation of China, Japan, and the Philippines in the Far Eastern Games

▲ China Officially Announces 26 Track and Field Athletes

▲ Japan Encourages the US and Australia to Join, Increasing Football Strength

▲ The Philippines Has No Hope of Victory in Baseball, Tennis, and Swimming Competitions

(1) Announcement of the Chinese Track and Field Team

The selection committee of the National Sports Association has selected 26 athletes to represent China in the track and field events of the Far Eastern Games and officially sent letters of notification yesterday. They are: Zhou Ende, Zhou Zhaoyuan, Yang Chuntai, Li Zhongsan (all from Tianjin); Zhong Lianji, Hao Chunde, Wang Jianwu, Deng Zhiming, Pan Nanshun, Ming Wang Jihui, Cao Yu (Shanghai); Liu Changchun, Lang Dakui, Jiang Yunlong, Zhao Dexin, Xiao Dinghua, Zhang Lingjia (Liaoning); Fu Baolu (Harbin); Zhao Wenrong, Lin Shaozhou (Fujian); Song Zean, Cheng Jinguan (Jiangsu); Mai Guozhen, Liang Xiaoping, Situ Guang (Guangdong). The Sports Association sent the following to the above athletes: "Dear Sir/Madam, the 9th Far Eastern Games will be held in Tokyo on May 24th. The review committee has selected you as a representative of the Chinese team. We hope that you will practice diligently so that your performance improves day by day. At that time, you will travel overseas, create new records, promote our national glory, and sing triumphant songs. We cannot express our anticipation enough."

(2) Japan Encourages the US and Australia to Join

The Far Eastern Games Rules Committee held a meeting at 7:00 PM on the 16th of this month at the Association's office in the Yaesu Hotel in Tokyo. Dr. Kish Kiyoshi, the president, chaired the meeting. Committee members Yamamoto, Noguchi, Sawada, Takashima, Yakushiji, and others attended. All the rules of the Games were discussed in detail. Seeing the gradual development of sports in China, Japan, and the Philippines, it was decided to expand the scope of the Games in the future and try to encourage the United States and Australia to join at the next Games. The name "Far Eastern Games" may not be practical in the future and should be changed to "Pan-Pacific Games." Japan decided to propose this suggestion at the upcoming tripartite meeting.

(3) Increased Strength of the Japanese Football Team

The strength of the Japanese football team has indeed greatly increased. Previously, they defeated the British warship HMS Woolwich (transliteration) of the Royal Navy 2-1 in Shanghai. This time, it cruised to Japan and docked in Yokohama. The Japanese football representatives participating in the Games, wanting to know the strength of our country, challenged the victorious British warship. The match was held at the Yokohama High School of Commerce ground at 1:00 PM on the 16th of this month. As a result, they drew 1-1. Japan is very proud of this, claiming that the British warship that defeated China could not defeat Japan. Through indirect comparison between China and Japan in football, Japan is superior to China.

(4) Holding a Japanese Traditional Swimming Competition

The Japan Swimming Federation has decided to add a public competition of Japanese traditional swimming to this Games. Therefore, it has hired many masters of traditional swimming schools. Those who have agreed to perform include the Mito Shinpa, Kobori, Mukai, Noshima, Iwakura, Tanouchi, and Kankai schools, eight schools in total. They will give public performances for thirty minutes every day from May 18th to May 31st. This type of sport will also be included in the program.

(5) Shortage of Baseball and Tennis Athletes in the Philippines

According to news from the Philippines, the representatives of the Philippine Islands for this Far Eastern Games were selected through the Carnival Athletics Meet in February of this year. Now that the Games are approaching, athletes from all over are gathering in Manila to prepare for intense training. Unexpectedly, there are difficulties in the baseball and tennis events due to the issue of participation. In early March, the Philippine Athletic Federation conducted a detailed review of the athletes in each event and then announced the names and teams of the representatives in the local newspapers. Two teams were selected as baseball representatives: the University of the Philippines and the Manila Student Association. Although these two teams are champions in the Philippines, their strength is too poor. Although our country's baseball is still immature, the Philippines' baseball is even worse than ours. Therefore, in every Games, the Philippine Islands are always defeated by our country. These two teams lack strong players, and recently many team members have requested leave. In addition, there is a shortage of coaching talent. Knowing that the outcome is important, the two teams jointly issued a statement to the Philippine Athletic Federation stating that they could not participate in the Games. It is said that there is still no solution to this matter, and the future is difficult to predict. Also, the tennis athletes who participated in the previous Games were the Holucson brothers. This year, the Holucson brothers were selected again. Both of them work for the railway bureau. Whether they can participate at that time depends on whether the railway bureau can grant permission. After these two incidents occurred, the Philippines was deeply worried, which is a sign of an unfortunate future. The reason is that the Philippines' selection of athletes is different from that of China and Japan. Except for track and field athletes, who are all students, the other athletes are not limited to professions. Therefore, the athletes selected this time are mostly employees of companies or shops, including Americans and Spaniards. (April 17th)

(6) Top Filipino Swimmer Breaks Off

The Philippine swimming representatives, a total of forty-nine candidates, had a final selection last week. Nine Moros were selected as official athletes because their performance was the best, excelling in the 50-meter, 100-meter, 400-meter, and 1500-meter freestyle. During the competition, the Filipinos' judging was unfair to them. Therefore, they sent a protest letter to the Philippine Athletic Federation, requesting the Athletic Federation to apologize, but it was rejected. The nine were enraged and announced their withdrawal from the Philippine delegation and could not participate in the Games. The Philippine Islands lost these nine top swimmers. Japan will dominate the swimming championships.

Local News

Changshu's Ban on Rice Exports Hinders the Food Supply of Shanghai Citizens

▲ The Municipal Government Cables the Jiangsu Provincial Government to Order the Lifting of the Ban

The Changshu County Government, under the pretext of a rice shortage, has banned the export of rice. The Joint Association of Rice Merchants in the Ningbo-Shanghai Cities and Counties of Jiangsu Province believes that this affects the source of rice for the city and has requested the municipal authorities to cable the Jiangsu Provincial Government to order the county to immediately lift the ban to maintain the people's food supply. Yesterday, it was learned that the municipal government has sent a cable to the Jiangsu Provincial Government to order the county to immediately abolish the measures banning rice exports. The original cable stated: "To the Jiangsu Provincial Government in Zhenjiang: According to the report of the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, the Joint Association of Rice Merchants in the Ningbo-Shanghai Cities and Counties of Jiangsu Province, including Ye Huijun, has reported that Changshu has banned the export of rice, obstructing the source of rice for the city, and requested that the report be forwarded to the Municipal Government, which would then forward it to the Jiangsu Provincial Government to order the lifting of the ban to maintain the people's food supply. It is noted that this year's rice production is poor, and there is fear of a food shortage. Shanghai is not a rice-producing area and relies on neighboring counties to help each other in times of urgency to stabilize the rice market and avoid social unrest. According to a letter from the Changshu Rice Merchants Association, a member of the association, the county government, under the name of relieving the rice shortage, has decided to ban the export of rice, and those who violate the ban will be intercepted and punished. If this resolution is implemented, not only will rice merchants in the county have no business to do, but the city's food supply will also be affected. If other counties follow suit, the source will be cut off, and how can the people survive? Looking ahead, we cannot help but shudder. Therefore, we specially request your review and forwarding to the Municipal Government, which would then forward it to the Jiangsu Provincial Government to order the county government to lift the ban immediately to maintain the people's food supply. According to this, it is noted that maintaining the circulation of grain within the country and prohibiting the hoarding of grain in domestic producing areas have long been ordered by the National Government to be followed by the provincial and municipal governments. According to your government's instruction No. 4040, in accordance with the order of the Executive Yuan, the Central People's Food Committee has replied to the review, and the problem of the people's food supply during the period of food scarcity in the city this year is also treated as a temporary measure, which is nothing more than circulating domestic grain to increase its source and prohibiting the export of grain overseas to curb its flow. If the local governments can strictly follow the two points of prohibiting hoarding and prohibiting private exports overseas, the food supply of Shanghai citizens will gradually increase. Now, the Changshu County Government, under the name of relieving the rice shortage, has banned the export of rice, which is in conflict with the central laws and regulations and greatly affects the city's food supply. Therefore, we specially request your Excellency to promptly cable the Jiangsu Provincial Government to order the Changshu County Government to immediately abolish the measures banning rice exports to maintain the food supply of the city, and we hope for a cable reply. We await with anticipation." The Shanghai Special Municipal Government (seal).

Rice Merchants Manipulating Imported Rice

▲ The Social Affairs Bureau Forbids Futures Trading

Recently, the market price of imported rice has continued to rise. The reasons for this are unknown to outsiders. Therefore, the findings of the investigation are recorded in detail below for the attention of those who are concerned about the people's food supply.

▲ Imported Rice Futures Trading The Shanghai Chinese Miscellaneous Grains, Oils, and Cakes Exchange originally planned to open trading in imported rice futures this spring, but because it did not obtain the approval of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, it changed to trading in the Miscellaneous Grains Association Market. Although there was no official auction in form, the buying and selling between the two parties was like a newly opened imported rice exchange. The Social Affairs Bureau did not pay attention at first and allowed it to operate freely, which led to general merchants, relying on their great economic power, buying in large quantities. For example, if you buy 100 tons of imported rice, you only need to pay a deposit of 1,000 taels. After a few months, the price of rice rises, and you can sell it off, netting 1,000 taels. Therefore, people outside the industry also believe that it is a shortcut to get rich. Seeing the continued soaring prices, they buy in early, hoard it, and wait for the price to rise. Those who have bought goods at low prices are already satisfied and have made a fortune by settling the transactions one after another. In recent months, the Chinese have all been long-term buyers, and the sellers have all been foreign merchants. Because the purchasing power of Chinese merchants is strong, prices have been rising steadily. However, the futures trading of imported rice in the public market has not decreased due to high prices. However, the use of a customer's purchase is entirely hoarding, not real sales. The rice market is a short-selling relationship, and it has soared. The highest price of No. 1 native rice has reached 22 yuan. As a result, the common people are suffering, while speculative rice merchants are making huge profits.

▲ The Prohibition Order of the Social Affairs Bureau It is now heard that the Social Affairs Bureau has found that the Miscellaneous Grains Association is suspected of manipulating and monopolizing the imported rice market. Therefore, yesterday, the association was ordered to stop new futures trading from today. The order is recorded below: "Order to comply. It is noted that the market price of imported rice has continued to rise recently, which has a significant impact on the livelihood of the common people. The director of this bureau has instructed Mr. Ye Huijun, the representative of the Equal Price Committee, to inform all his colleagues to temporarily suspend the resale of imported rice futures in order to avoid disrupting the market. It is hereby ordered that the association must earnestly warn its colleagues to comply and not to resell imported rice futures again, otherwise they will be severely punished. It is also necessary to find ways to stabilize the market price in order to maintain the people's food supply. You must report the compliance to be reviewed. This is of utmost importance." The merchants who depend on imported rice for their livelihood are worried. However, the spot goods of imported rice on the third floor of the association are naturally trading as usual. Regarding futures trading, it is heard that it is still being done secretly, but in smaller quantities. The spot market has been sluggish as a result.

Shanghai-Hangzhou Long-Distance Telephone

▲ Trial Call Yesterday

▲ Business to Begin Within Days

The long-distance telephone line between Shanghai and Hangzhou, built by the Ministry of Communications, started construction last winter and has been completed as of yesterday. Yesterday, engineers from the Hangzhou Telegraph Bureau and the Shanghai Telephone Bureau conducted a trial call, and the sound was very clear. It is heard that business will begin within one or two days. The long-distance telephone exchange is located in the Hangzhou Telegraph Bureau. The price list is as follows:

Zhejiang's First Group of Immigrants to Leave Tomorrow

▲ Approximately 800 People

Zhejiang Immigrants Head to Northeast to Cultivate Wasteland: The Zhejiang provincial government sent personnel to Shanghai to negotiate shipping arrangements with various shipping companies. The first group of immigrants is scheduled to depart for the Northeast, with the original plan to have them arrive in Liaoning by the end of this month. Over 300 people have already arrived in Shanghai. This matter has been reported repeatedly in this newspaper. Now, further details are provided below:

▲ Guangli to Go to Wenzhou for Transport: Most of the immigrants from Zhejiang province heading to the Northeast are from Wenzhou, Linhai, Yongjia, and other counties in eastern Zhejiang. According to reports from various counties, most are gathering in Wenzhou and have been arriving in succession. Yesterday, Zhou Botong, a member of the Shanghai Municipal Government responsible for this matter in Shanghai, received a telegram from Wenzhou stating that all the immigrants had arrived and requesting that a ship be sent immediately to transport them. Zhou then consulted with the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company. The company's business department relayed a telegram to the Guangli vessel, which was returning to Shanghai from Guangdong, instructing it to also call at Wenzhou today to transport this group of immigrants to Shanghai. It is estimated that they will arrive in Shanghai tomorrow.

▲ Initial Group's Number of Passengers: The Zhejiang government initially planned to send 1,500 people in the first batch. Therefore, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company originally intended to dispatch a dedicated ship to Wenzhou to directly load them and transport them to Yingkou for disembarkation. However, according to the telegram, the number of people reported from various counties only amounts to 60% of the original quota. In addition to the over 300 people who have already arrived, only about 500 more will be transported from Wenzhou to Shanghai tomorrow. The total will be only about 800 people leaving for the Northeast. It is expected that they will arrive in Yingkou on the 27th of this month. The Zhejiang provincial government has already telegraphed the Liaoning provincial government, requesting them to send personnel to take care of them upon arrival.

▲ Immigrants Leave Shanghai Tomorrow: The Huayang vessel, designated by the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to transport the immigrants to Yingkou, was originally scheduled to depart today. However, because the over 500 people carried by the Guangli vessel will not arrive in Shanghai today, the departure has been postponed for one day. They will wait in Shanghai, and once the immigrants are loaded onto the ship on the 23rd, they will sail directly to Yingkou. As the Zhejiang provincial government is facing economic difficulties, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company is offering free ship tickets for the immigrants traveling to Liaoning. Only a portion of the food expenses for each person will be collected. Additionally, the Zhejiang provincial government is requested to provide a partial subsidy for the ship's coal expenses. This matter has been agreed upon and will be handled accordingly.

Another Large Group of Chinese Citizens in Japan Expelled

The Japanese Consulate in Shanghai previously stated that Japan had no intention of excluding Chinese citizens. However, in recent days, numerous groups of Chinese laborers and merchants going to Japan have been expelled and sent back to China, totaling over 20 people. Among them are Cai Yuting, Ling Hansheng, Chen Lifa, and Cheng Keming, who were in the restaurant business and were heading to Kobe. However, they were stopped by the Japanese Maritime Police because they did not have entry permits. They were detained overnight and then sent back to Shanghai on the original ship. There are also He Xuanzhou, Chen Jinhe, Lin Youxiang, Hua Xinfu, and others who were detained in Osaka and sent back to Shanghai. Furthermore, Lin Jingshi, Chen Changji, and others were stopped in Nagoya and sent back to Shanghai. Even more, Huang Liudu, Wei Dongsong, Guo Zhoufu, Lin Songyuan, Xu Yindong, Weng Rengui, Zhang Dezheng, Lin Kongyin, and thirteen others were sent back from Tokyo. Moreover, two Fujianese people, Weng Youtian and Wang Jiajian, who secretly went to Japan, were discovered by the Japanese police in Nagasaki and also escorted to Shanghai. According to the Japanese side, Weng and Wang allegedly set up schemes in China to defraud Chinese people of money, claiming they could guarantee the entry of Chinese people into Japan. Many people were deceived and paid protection fees. After obtaining these funds, Weng and others secretly fled to Japan, but were unexpectedly discovered by the Japanese police. However, it is difficult to determine the accuracy of this information, as it comes from the Japanese.

Cooperation Between Chinese and French Police

▲ To Facilitate Arrests

The Da Wan Bao reports that detectives from the Public Security Bureau of the Special Municipality will have more freedom to work in the French Concession in the future when arresting criminals. This was decided at a joint meeting between the heads of the Public Security Bureau and the officers of the French Concession's police station. The results of the meeting have not yet been announced, but it is said that both sides agreed to cooperate and facilitate each other in pursuing kidnappers and armed robbers in the future. As for searching the residences of bandits, a simple phone call for assistance will suffice, and there is no need to go to the police station or the Public Security Bureau to apply, in order to be swift and beneficial to police work.

Military and Police Defense in May

In view of the large number of commemorative days in May, the military and police authorities in this port believe that it is necessary to plan ahead for prevention. The Songhu Garrison Headquarters convened a meeting of the heads of military and police organizations yesterday to discuss defense measures. The general idea is to divide the responsibilities by period, increase the number of military and police personnel, maintain public security, and organize a secret service team by the Public Security Bureau, assisted by armed soldiers dispatched by the Garrison Headquarters.
