Red Cross Society Opened Representatives' Meeting the Day Before Yesterday

▲ Passed the Constitution

▲ Election Today

The Third Membership Representatives' Meeting of the Chinese Red Cross Society was held on the 20th at the Heaven Queen Palace Bridge Business Consolidation Association. 128 branch representatives attended. Wang Yiting, Wang Peiyuan, Wen Lanting, Li Cishan, and Jiang Daqiu were publicly elected as the presidium, and Ji Heqin and Wei Ruifeng were the recorders. The full text of the charter is divided into ten chapters and sixty-one articles, including I. General Provisions, II. Association Affairs, III. Members, IV. Organization, V. Property, VI. Special Cases in Wartime and Disasters, VII. Branches, VIII. Protection, IX. Rewards and Punishments, and X. Supplementary Provisions. The charter was drafted by Red Cross Society standing councilors Lin Kanghou, Wang Xiaolai, and Wen Lanting, and jointly revised by Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting and the Ministers of Interior and Health. After that, it was reviewed by the charter review committee elected by the Red Cross Society's general assembly, Wen Lanting, Li Cishan, Jiang Daqiu, etc. During the general assembly, the representatives of each branch conducted a rigorous discussion. The main points were to change the president system to a committee system, with 49 standing councilors, 11 executive committee members, and 1 president. Departments such as documentation, disaster relief, medical affairs, and publicity were set up, and articles on poverty alleviation, infant care, and elderly care were added, which is about 60% to 70% more than the old charter. For finance, strict articles were included. The vote will be held this morning, and the proposals of each branch will be discussed in the afternoon.

Japan and the United States Compete for Pacific Aviation Rights

▲ Continue to Work Hard

▲ Six Osaka Ships Assigned: In order to compete in the Sino-US shipping industry, the Japanese Osaka Company built six new 9,000-ton oil-powered ships and assigned them to the Shanghai-New York route. The engine power of these six ships is extremely large. From Shanghai to New York, they can arrive within 35 days. The first ship will start its maiden voyage within August of this year and is currently being equipped with passenger seats. The six ships are named Di Hai Maru, Sanyo Maru, Kanto Maru, Kansai Maru, and the first one to start the route is Kinai Maru. Recently, the company has been planning to expand its export cargo business to the United States in Shanghai, Hankou, Tianjin, Qingdao, and other ports.

▲ Kawasaki Joins the Association: The current shipping competition in the Pacific is due to Japanese Kawasaki and other ships not joining the freight association. Therefore, they arbitrarily lower freight rates and are not bound by the association, causing lake silk freight rates to fall to one yuan per piece. Other goods are also reduced at will. British and American shipping companies in this port held several meetings to discuss countermeasures. It was agreed that the most appropriate fundamental solution was to persuade the Japanese company to join the association. However, after contacting them four times, there was no effect. It was confirmed yesterday that Kawasaki, after the fifth persuasion from British and American shipping companies, has agreed to join the Pacific Freight Association as a member. The company has 12 ships operating on the Pacific route. From now on, the company's freight rates cannot be increased or decreased freely and must be decided by the association through public discussion.

▲ The United States Increases New Ships: Since Nippon Yusen increased seven new ships in the Pacific this year, the US Maritime Commission believes that aviation rights are at stake and must be contested. It has been agreed that in the route from San Francisco to Shanghai, Qingdao, and other places, in addition to the original ships, it will add two more merchant ships that can travel at 14 knots per hour and carry 8,000 tons of cargo to expand to 17 trips per year. Also, in the route from San Francisco to Shanghai, including southern China, it will also speed up with two more merchant ships that can travel at 14 knots and carry 9,000 tons of cargo to expand to 19 trips per year and not allow the Japanese to gain exclusive advantages in transportation rights. Each new ship will be implemented starting next month.

▲ Latest News on Dollar's New Ships: In order to compete with British and Japanese shipping companies in the Sino-US shipping industry, American Dollar Steamship Lines built two large postal ships of 31,000 tons with 16 million US dollars. Construction began long ago, and one ship will be launched in August next year, specializing in the Shanghai-San Francisco route. The speed, cabin space, carrying capacity, etc. of each ship will exceed the three new ships of Nippon Yusen, such as Fushimi Maru. Each of the two ships is 653 feet long, 81 feet wide, and has a draft of 52 feet. It has 320 first-class rooms, 135 special-class rooms, and 800 third-class rooms. They are unprecedentedly large ships in the Pacific. The speed can reach 21 knots per hour. Two aircraft are also stationed on the ship for picking up and dropping off mail and passengers. The scale and beauty of the layout rank first among postal ships in the Far East.

Jing'an Carries Navy Cadets to Shanghai

▲ Ninety-seven Qualified

▲ Scheduled to Depart for Fuzhou on the 23rd

The naval transport ship Jing'an arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning from Beijing, carrying ninety-seven naval cadets who are being sent to the Fuzhou Naval Academy for study. The ship arrived at the port at 6:00 PM yesterday and docked at the Wusongkou. According to a certain adjutant surnamed Zhang who came to Shanghai on the same ship, speaking to the Daily News reporter, the naval recruitment examination in Beijing this time attracted approximately one hundred and sixty candidates for naval navigation and machinery, recommended by various provinces, cities, and overseas Chinese. After the physical examination by the recruitment committee, a total of one hundred and fourteen candidates were deemed qualified. Last week, they completed examinations in subjects such as Chinese, English, and arithmetic. After the examination, the recruitment committee sealed the students' examination papers and submitted them for evaluation. Acting Minister Chen convened all committee members, including Zeng Yiding, Li Shijia, and Wu Zhennan, for a plenary meeting to assess and determine the qualified students, totaling ninety-seven. In addition to announcements in newspapers in Beijing and Shanghai, Acting Minister Chen specially convened the admitted cadets the day before yesterday for a speech in the auditorium of the ministry, offering many words of encouragement. The cadets, led by Jing'an ship captain Ouyang Ji, boarded the ship. Yesterday morning, they set sail from Beijing to Shanghai. Tomorrow morning (i.e., this morning), Captain Ouyang will lead them ashore to visit the Shanghai Naval Shipyard at Gaochang Temple in the Nanshi, inspecting various factories, including the casting machinery factory, repair factory, and various dry docks, providing guidance. They will also briefly point out the main points of casting at the nearby arsenal and gun factory. Without much delay in Shanghai, they are scheduled to be sent to the Fuzhou Naval Academy for five years of study on the original ship tomorrow (the 23rd). After graduation, they will be sent to Europe and the United States for further studies to deepen their expertise. The future of talent in the naval sector of our country is immeasurable.

New Kang Ship Lawsuit Filed

After the merchant ship New Kang was sunk by a Japanese ship, negotiations have been ongoing for a long time without a resolution. The bureau submitted a request to the Ministry of Communications, which was approved. After filing a lawsuit in the Shanghai Special District Local Court, the bureau immediately entrusted a lawyer to submit a petition to the court, initiating legal proceedings and demanding that the defendant, the Japanese Mail Steamship Company, compensate for a loss of one million yuan. This lawsuit was not accepted previously due to the reorganization of the court. Now, it has been formally accepted and approved for trial. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs will notify the Japanese ambassador, ordering the company to appear in court for trial. The plaintiff has prepaid the litigation costs, which are guaranteed by Yu Qiaqing of the shipping association.

Land Survey of Zhabei District Commences

▲ Land Bureau Issues Notice to Landowners, Noting Four Points

The Municipal Land Bureau issued a notice yesterday, stating: "For the purpose of notification, the bureau is now beginning a land survey of households in the eleventh map of the twenty-seventh bao in the Zhabei District. Landowners should pay attention to the following items: (1) The land guarantor will distribute reporting forms to landowners. Landowners should truthfully fill them out within ten days of receiving the form, and the land guarantor will collect them and submit them to the Zhabei Survey Office of the bureau at the Xiajia Guanyintang on Qiujiang Road. (2) If the reporting form cannot be distributed due to the landowner's address being unknown, they can directly submit the filled form to the bureau or the survey office themselves. (3) If the landowner's land is mortgaged or pawned and they cannot fill in the name and acreage, they should promptly copy the information from the mortgagee or pawnbroker and not refuse to do so. (4) When the land of each household is measured, the landowner must, together with the land guarantor, clearly indicate the boundaries to the surveyor or measurement staff, or entrust a representative in advance to point out the boundaries on-site. Otherwise, the bureau will only rely on the land guarantor's instructions, and the landowner will be responsible for any errors or disputes that may arise in the future. The above four items are related to the consolidation of property rights for landowners and should be given special attention." This notice.

Ministry of Communications Cautious in Selecting Postal Personnel

The Directorate General of Posts and the Directorate General of Postal Savings and Remittances received Instruction No. 1055 from the Ministry of Communications yesterday, stating: "For compliance, it is noted that postal affairs and postal savings and remittance affairs are now managed separately by publicly established directorates general in accordance with the methods of various countries. The postal commissioners, assistant postal commissioners, deputy postal commissioners, chief accountants, and directors of first-class post offices in each district bear significant responsibility for postal and postal savings and remittance affairs. Therefore, their performance should be evaluated by both parties to ensure thoroughness. Hereafter, the performance evaluation of these personnel should be handled conscientiously by both directorates general. Any promotions, advancements, transfers, appointments, acting positions, or dismissals must be submitted to the ministry for approval by both directorates general. Furthermore, postal savings and remittance affairs are now being vigorously expanded, and the responsibilities of the postal commissioners and deputy postal commissioners are particularly significant. Therefore, when postal personnel are promoted to postal commissioners or deputy postal commissioners, careful selection of talent is essential to ensure they can perform their duties satisfactorily. Hereafter, both directorates general should conduct detailed assessments and submit a list of names to the ministry for approval before any promotions can be made. As for the current postal commissioners, assistant postal commissioners, deputy postal commissioners, chief accountants, and directors of first-class post offices in each district who also handle savings and remittance affairs, both directorates general should submit a list of names to the ministry for review and additional appointment with specific responsibilities. In addition to separate orders, you are to comply accordingly and instruct all subordinates to comply as well."

National Postal Union Petitions in Beijing

▲ Seeking Central Government Clarification on Four Key Points

Lu Jingshi, Zhao Shusheng, Wang Shufan, and Wang Yisheng, standing committee members of the National Postal Workers' Union, believing that the central government has misunderstandings regarding the union's organizational process and future work direction, and that the explicit order to temporarily suspend the union's activities is detrimental to postal affairs, traveled to Beijing the day before yesterday to petition the Central Training Department for clarification. They presented four key points: (1) Due to the uniformity of treatment systems and other matters for postal workers nationwide, the organization of a National Postal Workers' Union is necessary to avoid local disputes and ensure unified management. (2) In accordance with the special union organization regulations resolved by the 154th session of the Second Central Executive Committee, a preparatory committee was established on December 1, 1929. Due to the urgency of time, the union was unable to register with the central government. A request for registration has been submitted, and it is hoped that the central government will understand and approve the registration. (3) The Seamen's General Union has already been established. Postal workers also belong to the transportation sector and should be allowed to organize by analogy. (4) The preparatory committee's attitude is open and its purpose is pure. The central government should provide support to prevent reactionary elements from seizing the opportunity and causing unexpected disputes. It is reported that the committee members' petition in Beijing was very successful and will be resolved soon.

Chamber of Commerce Negotiates Against Heavy Tax on Parasols

Yesterday, the Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Jiangsu Finance Commissioner's Office and the Special Tax Bureau to negotiate against the heavy tax on parasols, stating: "Dear Sirs, On the 18th of this month, we received a letter from the Shanghai Special City Parasol Industry Consolidation Committee stating that the Huali Parasol Factory, a member of our committee, reported that at 5:00 PM on the 15th of this month, they shipped twenty dozen parasols to the Nanshi, intending to transport them to Haiyan. In accordance with past practice, they obtained a half-tax ticket from the Jiangsu Finance Department's Foreign Goods and Local Products Tax Bureau and a half-tax supplementary ticket from the Shanghai Tax Bureau's Nanshi Collection Office, which stated that the goods and ticket had been checked and verified by various tax offices and that an inspection certificate had been issued, exempting them from further taxation. However, the Cotton Special Tax Bureau, also under the Jiangsu Finance Department, suddenly sent people to seize the factory's parasols and refused to issue a receipt, demanding a fine of two yuan per dozen, totaling forty yuan. Our factory operates on a small scale and cannot afford this burden. This violates the principle of 'one item, one tax.' Considering that parasol raw materials include copper, iron, cotton, and wood, if each material is analyzed and taxed individually, domestic parasols will only face immediate bankruptcy. This runs counter to Dr. Sun Yat-sen's Principle of People's Livelihood and the National Government's advocacy of industry. Therefore, we urgently submit this appeal and request that you forward it to the superior authorities for assistance in negotiating the return of the seized parasols and the cancellation of this overlapping tax to save the parasol industry from danger. This would be most fortunate. The document and tax ticket are enclosed. Based on this, we have investigated the tax payment method for domestic parasols transported from this city to other locations. In the past, they have obtained a half-tax ticket from the Jiangsu Finance Department's Foreign Goods and Local Products Tax Bureau and a half-tax supplementary ticket from the Shanghai Goods Tax Bureau's Collection Office. After passing through various tax offices, they have been issued an inspection certificate and exempted from further taxation. This has been the established practice. Now that the Huali Parasol Factory has followed the established procedure, it should not be taxed again. Furthermore, the raw materials for parasols are made of cloth, iron, wood, etc., and taxes have already been paid at the Foreign Goods and Local Products Tax Bureau and the Goods Tax Collection Office. If they are also required to pay the cotton special tax, it would indeed be three or four taxes on one item, as the factory stated, leading to immediate bankruptcy. Taxing the only remaining domestic parasol industry with multiple taxes runs contrary to the purpose of protecting it. Moreover, the cotton special tax should apply to cotton textiles. If the parasols are taxed based solely on the cloth portion, then the fabric must have already been taxed by the piece goods merchant when it was woven and transported. There is no reason to pay the cotton special tax twice for the same cotton textile. If it is argued that parasols are a different type of item after being manufactured and cannot be compared to simple cotton textiles, then since parasols are not within the scope of the Goods Tax Office, there is no doubt that they are not under the jurisdiction of the Special Tax Bureau. Goods reported to the tax office are no longer subject to special taxes. This is a clear principle. Accordingly, we respectfully request that your office investigate and order the exemption from further taxation and the return of the twenty dozen seized parasols as soon as possible to protect domestic goods and relieve commercial difficulties. We eagerly await your response. Sincerely, To the Jiangsu Finance Commissioner's Office, the Jiangsu Special Tax Bureau's Cotton Special Tax Group."

Seeing that the officers were in high spirits and neatly dressed, especially with clean collar badges and hat trims, and that both internal and external duties were satisfactory, Director Yuan praised them greatly.

Local News 2

Kidnappers Use Guns in Broad Daylight

▲ In the Busy Area of Xinza Road

▲ Kidnappers Abduct Tang Zairu

▲ Chauffeur Shot Twice While Protecting Master

▲ Mrs. Tang Terrified, Attempts to Jump from Building

Yesterday at 9:30 AM, near the intersection of Xinza Road, Kader Road, and Xifukang Lane in the French Concession, four kidnappers shot and wounded chauffeur Lu Yonglin and abducted his master, Tang Zairu from Huzhou. The kidnappers took both the person and the car. The details obtained from the investigation are described below.

▲ Tang Zairu Kidnapped Upon Leaving Home: Tang Zairu, also known as Tang Ji, is a forty-two-year-old native of Huzhou residing at No. 1, Alley 5, Xifukang Lane, Xinza Road, with the house number being 617 and a half. He goes out on business every day and is very busy. He owns a car, with the Concession Permit number 4514, driven by Lu Yonglin from Changzhou. Yesterday morning at 9:30 AM, it was time for Tang to go out for business, but he was unexpectedly met by kidnappers upon leaving his home.

▲ Chauffeur Attempts to Drive Away in Emergency: Tang's chauffeur, Lu Yonglin, has been driving for Tang for a long time. Every day at 9:00 AM, he cleans the car and parks it at the entrance of Xifukang Lane, ready for his master's business trips. Yesterday, he parked as usual. At 9:30 AM, chauffeur's assistant Pan Hongcai came out to inform him that the master was about to leave and to prepare the car. Lu agreed, opened the car door, and started the engine. At this moment, Tang came out and boarded the car. Unexpectedly, four people jumped out from the alley entrance, shouting for them to stop. One of the kidnappers pulled out a gun, scaring chauffeur's assistant Pan Hongcai to the ground. Seeing the situation was bad, Lu Yonglin engaged the gear, trying to drive away from the dangerous situation.

▲ Kidnappers Angrily Fire Guns: The four kidnappers knew Tang would leave at this time, so they pretended to be pedestrians and lingered at the alley entrance. When they saw Pan Hongcai announce that the master had arrived, the kidnappers were already prepared and ready to abduct him. Seeing chauffeur Lu Yonglin engage the gear and try to escape, they thought they would be easily given up on a piece of fat meat about to enter their mouths. In this critical moment, they glared fiercely, pulled out their guns, two of the kidnappers used their guns to monitor Tang's actions, and stopped him from making any noise. The other two aimed at Lu's head and fired. Seeing the bullets, Lu immediately lowered his head, and the bullets flew over his head, fortunately missing him. However, one of the kidnappers, seeing that the bullet was avoided, fired another shot, hitting Lu's left shoulder. The bullet passed through his back.

▲ Kidnappers Shout "Kidnapping" and Flee with Person and Car: The Xifukang Lane area is lined with shops and is adjacent to the Kader Road Triangle Market. Every morning, vendors and shoppers with baskets pass by, resembling the bustling scene of Shanyin Road. Pedestrians heard two gunshots and were wondering what was happening when they suddenly heard shouts of "Catch the kidnappers," with strained voices. Amidst the noise, the kidnappers forced the chauffeur into the middle seat and drove away quickly, heading east. Onlookers shouted "Kidnapping" and followed to the Kader Road intersection, where they saw the car head south and turn onto Rue Amiral Courbet, heading west. It is believed they fled to western Shanghai. At that time, the chauffeur's assistant saw that the kidnappers had gone far and dared to report to Tang's wife.

▲ Injured Man Abandoned in Wasteland: After the kidnappers took the person and car, chauffeur Lu Yonglin, although shot in the back, remained conscious but could not bear the pain and shouted for help. The kidnappers, fearing something would happen on the way, covered his mouth to prevent him from speaking. The hostage, Tang Zairu, was also squeezed tightly by two kidnappers, wearing dark glasses, and was not allowed to make any noise, otherwise he would be killed immediately. When the car reached the western part of Route Doumer, near Jing'an Temple, the area became desolate, with green trees and few pedestrians. The four kidnappers abandoned Lu Yonglin on the wasteland, got back in the car, and sped away.

▲ Sent to Hospital, Life in Danger: Chauffeur Lu Yonglin, after being abandoned on the wasteland of Route Doumer, shouted for help with all his might. However, due to his serious injuries, he could not walk. Later, a villager heard the sound and reported to the nearby patrol, who sent him to the Red Cross Hospital on Route Haig. Doctors performed surgery to remove the bullet. According to the doctor, his condition is quite dangerous. If there are no changes in two or three days, his life can be saved. The detectives from the Route Tenant de la Tour Police Station obtained a brief statement from him when he regained consciousness and learned about the kidnapping. They then telephoned the Gorden Road Police Station to conduct a thorough investigation.

▲ Mrs. Tang Suffers a Nervous Breakdown: When reporters arrived at Tang's residence to inquire, the family asked them not to make any noise because Mrs. Tang had suffered a nervous breakdown upon hearing the news, fearing she would jump out the window. According to the family, there were no prior threats or letters before Tang's kidnapping. He has no savings in his life, and others mistakenly believe he is wealthy because he owns a car, but the car was given to him by a friend. The family of four relies on him for their livelihood. His eldest daughter, age twenty-one, is studying at the Nanyang Girls' High School. His second daughter, age fourteen, is also studying with her sister. His son, age six, is still playing. His wife, surnamed Jiang, is thirty-seven years old and is suffering from a nervous breakdown.

▲ Empty Car Found in the French Concession: After Tang was kidnapped, the Gorden Road Police Station dispatched Chinese and Western detectives to the scene to conduct a detailed investigation. They also notified all police stations and the North and South Public Security Bureaus to pay attention to the car with the number 4514. At 5:30 PM, the French police telephoned the Gorden Road Police Station, saying that the empty car had been found on Rue Pére Froc. The car body was not damaged.

Assistant Drives Car Without Permission, Leading to Uncontrollable Consequences

Detailed Report on Automobile Accident Resulting in Six Deaths and Injuries

▲ Assistant Had No Driver's License

▲ Speeding Without Honking Horn

▲ A Major Tragedy Unfolds in an Instant

▲ Attempt to Abandon Car and Flee After the Accident

Yesterday's newspaper reported on a car accident resulting in multiple deaths and injuries. The following is a continuation of the detailed report on the accident and the court's interrogation yesterday.

▲ Tan Xinzhen's Car: After the reorganization of the Provisional Court, former Judge Tan Xinzhen has resumed his career as a lawyer. The afternoon before yesterday, as his eldest son's wedding was approaching, Tan hired his own car, number 3867, to go to the Yipinxiang Hotel on Tibet Road to book a room for the auspicious occasion. Upon arriving at the hotel, Tan got out of the car and went inside, instructing his chauffeur, Chen Xiaosi, to drive the car home.

▲ Car Becomes Uncontrollable: Chen drove the car to Zhejiang Road and got out to buy shoes, parking the car at the intersection of Tianjin Road, instructing his assistant, Zhang Cheng, to watch over it. Unexpectedly, Zhang drove off on his own, speeding excessively. As he drove along Tianjin Road and Guizhou Road, people scattered out of the way. Zhang had no driving experience, leading to uncontrollable consequences.

▲ Indeed, a Major Disaster Occurred: As a result of the speeding, one person, Jiang Bainian, was killed, and five people were injured: Zhu Peiyuan, Cai Shunheng, Jiang Changlin, Tang Desheng, and Cai's wife, Cai Abao. The Laozha Police Station sent detectives to arrest the culprit, Zhang Cheng, and the chauffeur, Chen Xiaosi, and took them to the police station. Jiang Bainian's body was taken to the coroner's office on Fielun Road.

▲ Life and Death Uncertain: Zhu Peiyuan and the others were sent to the hospital for treatment. After examination and medication by the doctors, Jiang Changlin's injuries were minor, and he was discharged from the hospital soon after. The remaining four suffered serious injuries. According to the doctors, it is difficult to predict whether there is any danger to their lives and must wait until Saturday of this week to be certain.

▲ Prosecution According to Criminal Law: Yesterday morning, the police, along with Jiang Changlin, escorted Zhang and Chen to the Special District Local Court, where Judge Sun Yuan presided over the first hearing. The police lawyer, Gan, presented the facts and charged them with causing death by injury under Article 291 of the Criminal Law and with injury under Articles 293 and 295. Zhang Cheng was also charged with violating Article 34 of the Municipal Council's regulations for driving without a license.

▲ Statement of the Chinese Constable: Subsequently, Chinese Constable No. 1103 reported the situation at the time, stating that he was on duty near the scene of the accident when he suddenly heard a crash and saw the defendant, Zhang Cheng, abandoning the car and fleeing from north to south, whom he caught.

▲ Speeding Without Warning Signal: Witness Zhao Boyi testified that he worked at a cigarette paper shop behind the Xian Shi Company and saw the car speeding from the north, knocking down a man, a woman, and a child in succession. Witness Hong Zaiyu testified that he was passing by and saw the defendant, Zhang Cheng, driving the car at high speed without honking the horn. In an instant, three people were knocked down.

▲ Report of the Western Constable: Western Constable No. 309 stated that yesterday afternoon at 4:40, he came out of the police station and passed by the area, where he saw a person trapped under the car, as well as an old man and a young man who were injured. Upon investigation, in addition to these three, two more people were injured, and one person was killed. The car had no driver in it at the time of the accident.

▲ Let It Go Where It Will: Judge Sun interrogated Chen Xiaosi, who confessed that he was from Jiangbei and worked as a chauffeur for the Tan Residence. Zhang Cheng was previously an apprentice and is now learning to be a driver with him and that this has lasted for three months. Zhang Cheng confessed that he was from Shandong and drove the car on Tianjin Road at 4:50 PM on the 20th. The car was originally driven by Chen, but since Chen stopped there, he slightly adjusted the machinery and unexpectedly the car drove off and he was unable to stop it, so he let it go where it will, feeling very flustered and causing the accident. He had not obtained a driver's license. Chen and Zhang both hired lawyers Fan Gang and Liang Bohua for their defense. Judge Sun then ordered Chen Xiaosi to provide a guarantee of 500 yuan from a reputable shop and remanded Zhang Cheng in custody, scheduling another hearing in seven days.

▲ Coroner's Examination of the Deceased: After ten o'clock, Court Inspector Guo visited the scene to examine Jiang Bainian's body. He interviewed the Western constable and Jiang Changlin, son of the deceased and injured at the same time, and inquired about the situation. He instructed Jiang to collect the body and make funeral arrangements. Accidents involving cars in Shanghai occur every day, so they are common sight, but an incident resulting in six deaths and injuries in a row is rare.

Young Man Commits Suicide by Poisoning, Claiming Economic Oppression

▲ Deceased Worked at Paris Dance Hall

▲ Fired for Embezzling Over a Thousand Yuan

▲ Lodged at the Oriental Hotel Before Death

▲ Visited by Prostitute

The day before yesterday, a suicide occurred at the Oriental Hotel on Tibet Road. The deceased was named Chen Kepei. On the morning of the 18th, Chen went alone to the Oriental Hotel and checked into Room 307, with no possessions. Later, a female guest visited him. According to the hotel attendant, she saw the female guest, whose appearance and behavior were very much like that of a prostitute. Chen and the female guest left together, and Chen returned alone in the afternoon. In the evening, before going to bed, there was nothing unusual. At 9:00 AM the next morning, the attendant entered Room 307 to clean and saw Chen lying stiffly on the bed, no longer breathing. He reported to the Laozha Police Station, who sent a detective to investigate. Two letters were found near the deceased, one addressed to Mao Yongchang, manager of the Paris Dance Hall, referring to Mao as "Master," and the other addressed to his parents. The letter stated that the suicide was entirely due to environmental and economic pressures. In addition, one yuan in silver, two dimes, and a gold watch, cigarette case, and other items were left behind. The detective took the body to the morgue on Fielun Road. Yesterday morning, the Special District Local Court was requested to send Court Inspector Guo to the morgue to examine the body. It was not possible to determine what poison Chen Kepei had taken to cause his death. Mao Yongchang and others were summoned by the police. According to Mao, Chen was his student and was recently suspended due to embezzling more than a thousand yuan, while the details of the embezzlement were being investigated. He said that Chen's suicide was the result of his recklessness. Later, the Oriental Hotel attendant testified about Chen's lodging, and Wu Zhiwen arrived to state that the deceased was his cousin. Finally, the Western constable presented the letters, the gold watch, two yuan, and three empty opium boxes found near the deceased. Court Inspector Guo ordered the investigation to continue next Tuesday (today).

Open-Air Meeting of Sixty or Seventy People on Vacant Land

▲ Patrolmen Arrived and They Scattered in All Directions

▲ Six People Were Arrested and Leaflets Were Seized

▲ A Tram Window Was Smashed

▲ Interrogation Yesterday by the Higher Branch Court

In the vacant lot in front of the Sanxing Cotton Mill at 87 Yangshupu Road, at 9 a.m. the day before yesterday, a group resembling workers held an open-air meeting. The Municipal Public Security Bureau had received a report beforehand. As the location was in the foreign concession, they specifically notified the political department of the Chief Inspector's Office by telephone to take precautions to prevent reactionary elements from taking the opportunity to incite trouble. The Chief Political Department dispatched Western Detective Arok, along with Chinese Detective Zhang Yunjian, to investigate. Upon arrival, they saw sixty or seventy people gathered. Several people in Western suits and long gowns were leading them. As soon as these people saw the Chinese and Western detectives, they scattered in all directions and many fled. The detectives immediately arrested He Qingxiang from Sichuan, Yao Guanghua from Anhui, Li Longzhi from Beiping, Chen Jiaxing from Zhejiang, Yan Zhaotang from Ningbo, and Song Chaowei from the local area, a total of six people. They seized a bundle of leaflets filled with reactionary text and took them to the police station for detention. Because the case involved counter-revolution, they were specifically sent to the Second Tribunal of the Higher Branch Court yesterday morning, where Judge Ye Zaizhou opened a preliminary hearing. The police lawyer, Ru Baoyi, stated first that they could be prosecuted under Articles 103, 157, and 160, etc., of the Criminal Code. However, after the defendants were arrested, the Municipal Public Security Bureau sent a representative to the police station, requesting that they be transferred to the Public Security Bureau. The power to transfer rested with the court, so they were specifically brought to the court for review. No representative from the Public Security Bureau was present in court today. However, the case occurred and the arrests took place within the foreign concession, so the court had jurisdiction. Moreover, except for Yao Guanghua, who resided on Jiangxi Road, the rest lived in the Chinese area, so the inland authorities could also handle the case. If they insisted on taking them away, they should be handed over to the inland judicial authorities for a joint trial. Next, Western Detective Arok reported the circumstances of the defendants' arrest, stating that at 9:05 a.m. yesterday morning, they received a telephone report that communists were holding a meeting in front of the Sanxing Cotton Mill. He and the Chinese detectives rushed there and saw sixty or seventy people gathered on the vacant lot, holding a meeting. When the defendants Li Longzhi and the three people in Western suits saw them, they fled towards Lan Road. He gave chase for a long time and finally caught Li on Huaxing Road. The three men in Western suits had escaped towards the Chinese area. The other five defendants were arrested by the Chinese detectives. At 9:30 a.m., they received a telephone report from the British-American Tramway Company that a tram, which had passed in front of the Sanxing Cotton Mill before 9:30 a.m., had one of its window panes broken by the crowd with violence. The company had sent a representative to the case and could testify. Judge Ye then interrogated each of the defendants separately. They all denied the accusations. Later, a Westerner from the tram company made a few statements. The court ordered the defendants to be remanded to custody and rescheduled the hearing for further investigation.

Gun and Ammunition Discovered by Chance

▲ Due to Carrying a Large Sum of Money

▲ The One-Legged Bandit Was Alarmed by a Half-Price Ticket

On the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway express train from Shanghai to Hangzhou, at around 9 a.m., when soldiers were about to inspect passenger tickets at Longhua Station, they suddenly discovered a large sum of yarn tickets and military ammunition. The following is a summary of what was seen:

▲ Oil Factory Accountant Carrying a Large Sum of Money Yesterday, when the Shanghai-Hangzhou express train departed from Shanghai, an oil factory employee came to Shanghai and collected more than 4,000 yuan in cash. He boarded the train to return to Zhejiang. Unexpectedly, two bandits secretly carried two new-style pistols, each one foot and two inches long, and more than six hundred bullets, and boarded the same train.

▲ Child's Ticket Caused Alarm After the express train left Longhua Station, the ticket inspector proceeded to check passenger tickets one by one. When he reached the bandits who were carrying firearms, because the bandit was accompanied by a child over ten years old who had not purchased a ticket, the inspector instructed him to buy a supplementary ticket. One of the bandits suddenly became alarmed. The inspecting soldiers carried out a search and found a pistol and bullets on the one-legged bandit's waist (the bandit had only one leg and used a wooden crutch for support). After the two bandits were arrested, it was learned that they were following the person carrying the money.

▲ Bundles of Cash Wrapped Around the Waist The inspecting soldiers then summoned the person carrying the large sum of money and asked him to take the money out of the pouch around his waist. The person claimed to be an accounting employee of an oil mill, who came to Shanghai to collect accounts and was returning. However, he did not know the railway regulations and could not carry so much cash, etc. Therefore, the inspecting soldiers took the two arrested bandits, along with the person carrying the money, and all the seized military ammunition, to the authorities for interrogation.

Jardine, Matheson & Co. Initiates a Far East Travel School

▲ The Evening News reported that Jardine, Matheson & Co. recently initiated a Far East Travel School. It will gather teachers and students in the United States and take advantage of the summer vacation to combine travel with academic research. It is scheduled to depart from Seattle on June 15, travel around major cities in China, Japan, and the Philippines, and return to the United States on August 23. If the route takes them via Honolulu, it will be extended to September 3. In China, they plan to visit Beijing, Tianjin, Shanghai, Nanjing, Hong Kong, Guangzhou, and other ports. All expenses along the way are included, and the fee is 1,310 US dollars per person. Jardine, Matheson & Co. has now hired Flora, the principal of Roosevelt High School in Seattle, as the director.

Reconstruction of the Seeker Lighthouse at the Wusong Fortress

Deng Zhenquan, the commander of the Wusong Fortress, considering that the original seeker lighthouse had low horsepower and insufficient range, and that it might not be effective during searches, ordered a new 25-horsepower German engine and transported it to the fortress. He then ordered the lighthouse to be rebuilt. It is now learned that the project is nearing completion. Yesterday afternoon, Commander Deng, accompanied by Chief of Staff Teng, went to inspect the site to review whether there were any improper installations, and ordered the project to be completed soon so that it could be tested.

Director Wu duly submitted the situation to the Jiangsu Construction Department for review. Now, instructions have been received requiring the company to register in advance. Yesterday, the bureau instructed the company to comply.

Nishi Hongwanji Temple Held Groundbreaking Ceremony Yesterday

The Nishi Hongwanji Temple, established by Japanese residents in Shanghai, is the only religious institution for the 25,000 Japanese residents in Shanghai. Recently, the temple raised a large amount of funds and purchased land to build a new temple. At 11 a.m. yesterday, a groundbreaking ceremony was held at the new site at the corner of Laobazi Road and Zhapu Road. The venue was newly decorated. Thousands of Chinese and Japanese people from all walks of life attended the ceremony. Chinese and Japanese officials and gentry who participated in the groundbreaking ceremony included Tang Shaoyi, Xiong Shihui, Zhang Qun, Mamoru Shigemitsu, Saito, Fukushima, Hayashi Ideo, and Hayashi Yūkich, and dozens of others. Shigemitsu, representing the ambassador, wielded the hammer to lay the foundation. Construction committee member Oda and others erected the cornerstone. Hayashi Yūkich and Saito delivered congratulatory speeches. The meeting adjourned at 2 p.m.

Women's Sightseeing Tour Group from Weiting Mountain Arrives in Shanghai

Improving rural life requires improving peasant families as a key measure. The rural service department of the Weiting Mountain Youth Association, in view of this, specially organized a women's sightseeing tour group of fifteen people. They obtained a half-price discount from the Beijing-Shanghai Railway. Led by secretary Chen Ruzhen, they came to Shanghai the day before yesterday to sightsee, to increase their knowledge, invigorate their spirits, and enable them to innovate in everything after returning to their hometown. Mr. Huang Chujiu also gifted them free tickets to visit the Great World, allowing them to enjoy the sights to their hearts' content. Today, they plan to visit a chicken farm and other places in Jiangwan.

Dr. Bando Visits Shanghai-Hangzhou Leprosy Hospitals

Dr. Bando, head of the leprosy section of the Health Department of the League of Nations, arrived in Shanghai on the President Cleveland on the morning of the 18th of this month from Tokyo. The afternoon before yesterday, Li Yuanxin, president of the China Leprosy Relief Association, Vice President Diao Xinde, Executive Secretary Wu Zhijian, and others invited him to visit the leprosy clinic at 173 Linping Road in the Hongkou Public Society, which the association had recently taken over. Dr. Bando expressed his approval of the clinic and said that such clinics are excellent tools for eliminating leprosy. However, Shanghai still needs a new-style leprosy hospital to provide accommodation. Dr. Bando visited the Guangji Leprosy Hospital in Hangzhou yesterday and returned to Shanghai immediately. He took the 11 o'clock overnight express train to Beijing to visit Minister of Health Dr. Liu Ruiheng and senior government officials, urging them to find ways to eliminate leprosy in China as soon as possible.

Reactionary Crimes and Robbery Crimes

▲ The Cases of Each Defendant Will Be Tried Separately

Since the reactionary organization at 1132 Tongchun Lane, Gongping Road, was raided by the Hongkou police, and forged seals and forged letters of appointment were seized, and Lin Jinhan, a native of Tongzhou, was arrested, nine male and female accomplices have been arrested one after another. However, most of them are related to the robbery case. Except for Yu San, who escaped while being led by detectives to the Bao Yu Lane in the French Concession to recover stolen goods, there are still eight people remaining. They are being detained at the police station awaiting investigation and interrogation. This has been reported in this newspaper repeatedly. The day before yesterday, another local named Wu Asan was arrested by the Chinese and Western detectives handling the case. Yesterday morning, Lin Jinhan, Zhao Jiaying, Zhang Bingsheng, Zhang Wangshi, Nie Changfu, Bao Yongchang, Wu Rongsheng, Lin Qiaoyun, and other eight male and female defendants who were in custody were sent to the Second Tribunal of the Higher Branch Court. Judge Ye Zaizhou took the bench and ordered that the defendants, except Wu Rongsheng, Lin Qiaoyun, and Wu Asan, be brought forward for a further preliminary hearing. Because the parts of the charges against Lin Shuanghan and Zhao Jiaying that relate to internal disorder still need to be investigated, it was ordered that they be remanded to custody along with Zhang Bingsheng and Zhang Wangshi. Yan Changfu and Bao Yongchang were charged with robbery and it was ordered that they be transferred to the Special District Local Court for trial. After the order was given, the court recessed. Then, Judge Gao Junxiang took the bench and ordered Wu Rongsheng, Wu Asan, and the woman Lin Qiaoyun to be brought to the case for preliminary trial. They did not belong to the jurisdiction of the Higher Branch Court, and it was ordered that they be transferred to the Special District Local Court for trial. After the order was given, he also left the bench, and the defendants were still detained separately.

A Large Number of Fishing Boats Arrived in Wusong Yesterday

▲ More Than Five Hundred Pirates on the High Seas

▲ Fishing Boats Severely Harassed

The northern yellow croaker fishing boats from Wusong, after the Chen Shunxing boat from Cuisheng Fish Company arrived the day before yesterday (the 18th), all the fish companies thought that the other boats would arrive in Wusong continuously, and they all eagerly awaited them. It was not until the night before last that ten fishing boats, Wang Zengxing, Wang Heshun, Xu Liantai, Xu Fulong, Xu Wantai, Zhang Jixing, Jin Xulong, Xu Hefeng, Zuo Zengmao, and Chu Changlong, sold by Baofeng Fish Company, arrived in Wusong. Yesterday morning, more than ten boats, including Xu Hetai and Peng Jinfa, arrived. In one day, a total of twenty-five or six fishing boats arrived. Baofeng opened the market at nine catties per share. However, because the southern yellow croaker market has been crowded in recent days and the market has been sluggish, each customer demanded to increase it to nine and a half catties. Therefore, the hatch could not be opened in the morning. The customers from both upstream and downstream argued fiercely. It was not until the afternoon that they agreed on nine and a half catties, and each customer began to unload their boats and sell their goods. However, according to people in the fishing boats, more than five hundred pirates were discovered on the fishing waters this year. They demanded fees from each fishing boat, eighty yuan per boat. Those who had cash on board were allowed to fish after paying the fee. If they did not have cash, they would have their fish or cargo robbed after they caught the fish, or they would share it with the pirates. Therefore, none of the arriving boats were full of fish. Each boat owner complained incessantly about the difficulties of doing business. Two boats, Quan Tongchang and others, each caught two holds of spring fish, and all of their cargo was looted. Businessmen generally hope that the authorities will take measures to stop this, so as to help the merchants who are struggling to maintain the fishing industry.

Farmers Tormented by Foul Odor

▲ Collapsed on the Grave Mountain All Night

▲ Discovered Yesterday Morning by Passersby

Su Yixiang, a farmer from Sujiazhai, northwest of Wusong, 34 years old, left his home at about 3 p.m. the day before yesterday to collect club funds from his relative, Zhang's, home. Su's family waited until about 12 o'clock the night before last, but Su still had not returned home. Su's house was three miles away from Zhang's house. Fearing that Su might have encountered thieves on the way, they immediately sent many people to Zhang's house to inquire. According to Zhang's, Su arrived at Zhang's house, but at about 8 p.m., the club funds were not yet complete, so Su said that he would go to collect the money again the next morning, and then walked home. Su's family heard this and were very surprised, so they split up and went to visit relatives and friends everywhere to find him. However, there was no trace of him. It was not until about 6 a.m. yesterday morning that a farmer, Chen Xiaodi, went to the town market and saw Su collapsed on the side of the road on the grave mountain. Because he was familiar with him, he stepped forward to look at him and found that Su was groaning non-stop, as if he was sick. He immediately went to Su's house to report. Su's family went and carried Su back, and gave him ginger soup and other things to drink. It was not until about 9 a.m. that Su's mind gradually became clear. The family asked him why he was lying on the grave. Su said that after leaving Zhang's house the night before, it was already dark. He was walking on the road when he suddenly smelled an indescribable foul odor in his nose, and his mind suddenly became blurred. He did not know how he collapsed in the graves. Now, Su's spirit has returned to normal, and there are no signs of illness. Since this incident occurred, the farmers in the vicinity of the area believe that there must be a poisonous substance at work. Yesterday afternoon, they invited many people to go to the area near where Su collapsed to search, but no poisonous substance was found.

Inquiries About Water Connection in the Fahua District

The residents of Yangcun, Fahua District, West Shanghai, have always obtained their drinking water from the Shangao Pond. Last year, citizens Shi Zongtang and He Lanqing, etc., complained that the pond water was dirty and unsuitable for drinking. They planned to unite the villagers and raise funds to purchase water pipes and faucets to connect to the Hongqiao Road water pipes and temporarily purchase water from the Shanghai Waterworks Company. The municipal committee of the Fahua District reported the information to the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau for review. After consideration, the bureau believed that it would harm sovereignty for citizens to directly use the foreign concession's tap water. In order to avoid future disputes, it did not approve the request. The bureau has now established limited measures for Chinese residents requesting access to the foreign concession's water and electricity, stipulating that temporary access will be permitted, but a written statement must be provided, stating that when the Chinese water and electricity lines arrive in the future, they will immediately switch to the Chinese water and electricity. The written statement has been sent to the committee member. If citizen Shi Zongtang and others still need to connect to tap water, the committee member can instruct them to fill out the written statement for verification.

Change of Detention Order for Zhang Wenzheng in the Bigamy Case Yesterday

Zhang Wenzheng (also known as Zhang Yunqing), a compradore of the insurance department of the Arnhold, Karberg & Co. from Nanxiang, was criminally charged with bigamy and abandonment by his wife Zhang Luoqingfen. The Special District Local Court had previously opened a hearing, but the defendant did not appear. It was ordered that the plaintiff lead the bailiffs to point out the defendant for another interrogation. This has been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Wu Tingqi opened a hearing, but the defendant still did not appear. The co-defendants Luo Cuiyun and Li Qitang also did not appear despite being summoned. According to the report from the Chinese bailiffs who went to serve the summons, they went to 1112 Xinping Lane, Longmen Road, the day before yesterday to summon Li Qitang, but his family claimed that Zhang Wenzheng did not live there, so Zhang could not be reached. Then, Li Qitang's son, Li Changyi, stated that although Zhang Wenzheng was his uncle-in-law, he really did not know his address. However, his aunt lived in Nanxiang, and his father could not appear in court today due to illness. After hearing Li's son's statement, the plaintiff, Luo Qingfen, claimed that Zhang Wenzheng was definitely living with Li. The lawyer for the plaintiff also claimed that Zhang and Li were both compradores at Arnhold, Karberg & Co. and definitely lived together, which clearly showed that they were intentionally avoiding the summons. She requested detention. The court granted the request, and the case was adjourned again.

Mistress Kills Paramour

▲ The Murderer Fled ▲ Implicated the Husband

Yuan, the wife of Cao Erlang, a native of Chongming, who lived in the Lu Xuejia House in the Chinese area of West Shanghai, Whitelee Road, was naturally promiscuous. She first had an affair with Xue Arong, who lived in the same house. At first, their relationship was quite harmonious, but later, she had an affair with Tang Agen, and they were very intimate, going out and traveling together without any scruples. Xue saw them several times and was consumed by anger, which led to the tragedy due to jealousy. The day before yesterday, Xue Arong carried a sharp axe, found Zhao, and chopped him with the axe. Zhao was chopped several times on the head and body, and blood flowed into a ditch. Zhao collapsed in a pool of blood. Xue saw that his goal had been achieved and fled without a trace. Later, the police arrived and sent Zhao to the nearby Chinese Red Cross Hospital on Hager Road for treatment. Unfortunately, he was seriously injured and could not be saved. He died soon after. The local court has been notified to send someone to examine the body. The police have detained Cao Erlang and Yuan, the husband and wife, and sent them to the court for investigation, and they are tracking down the murderer Xue Arong to bring him to justice.

Mother-in-Law and Daughter-in-Law Appeared in Court

▲ Mother-in-Law Sued Daughter-in-Law for Assault

▲ Aftermath of the Dispute Over Five Hundred Yuan

The woman, Xu Chen, previously sued her mother-in-law, Yan Cao, in the Shanghai Local Court for not paying a deposit of five hundred yuan. Yan Cao submitted a defense, stating that the deposit belonged to her daughter, Xu Yan (i.e., Xu Chen's daughter-in-law), so she refused to pay it. A judgment was then issued, determining that Yan Cao had lost the case. Therefore, Xu Chen hired a lawyer and also filed a separate lawsuit with the court, stating that her husband, Xu Jialong, had died in 1915, leaving a son, named Xiliang, who was only three years old. She had a private savings of 1,900 yuan, which she deposited in her mother's home in 1922 to earn interest for living expenses. Last October, she returned to Ningbo for some reason, and her savings passbook was taken away by her aunt, Xu Chen. Now, after continuous withdrawals, there is still 500 yuan left in the deposit. She intends to use it to marry a daughter-in-law. She requested that it be awarded to her so that she could withdraw it. As a result, the deposit was allowed to be withdrawn by Xu Yan. At noon on February 27 of this year, after the court hearing, the mother-in-law and daughter-in-law, Xu Chen and Xu Yan, left the court. A conflict arose on the way. The next day, Xu Chen went to the prosecutor's office of the Local Court to criminally sue her daughter-in-law, Xu Yan, for assaulting her. After investigation, the criminal court was convened and requested a public trial. Yesterday morning, Judge Deng opened a hearing. The plaintiff, Xu Chen, hired lawyer Sha Xunyi to appear in court and make a statement, while the defendant, Xu Yan, also hired lawyer Ma Junshuo to defend her. The mother-in-law and daughter-in-law appeared in court. Xu Chen stated first that after leaving the court on February 27, her daughter-in-law, Xu Yan, twisted her arm with her hand. When they returned home to the Jiuxiaochang, Dong Kaiqi came to her house and committed assault. She asked for investigation. Xu Yan stated that the former civil litigation led to a situation where, after leaving the court, the mother-in-law grabbed her and demanded the 500 yuan deposit. She bit her own arm and falsely accused her of hitting her. She asked for a review. She was asked what Dong Kaiqi was to her and answered that he was a relative of her sister. Dong Kaiqi claimed to be in the porcelain business. He was passing by Jiuxiaochang that day and saw Xu Yan's son, Xiliang, crying at the door. He asked and learned that there was a dispute between the mother-in-law and daughter-in-law, Xu Chen and Xu Yan. He entered to mediate and did not commit any assault. Xu Xiliang claimed to be seventeen years old. Xu Chen was his grandmother and Xu Yan was his mother. He testified that his mother did not hit his grandmother. After the lawyers on both sides argued, it was ordered that the debate be concluded and that they wait for the verdict. They then left the court.

Ji Sheng Hui's Zhang Xianqing to Depart for Shaanxi Today to Handle Disaster Relief

Mr. Zhang Qing, director of the China Ji Sheng Hui's Shaanxi relief efforts, previously returned to Shanghai from Xi'an to raise funds and personally reported on the severity of the disaster to Lu, stating that it was a critical period between harvests when people could not survive without rice. He personally witnessed the tragic situation, which was reported in newspapers. He originally intended to return to Shaanxi Province immediately to plan relief efforts, but was delayed due to road obstacles and various other reasons. Now, Director Zhang believes that the Shaanxi disaster must be addressed, or else the opportunity will be lost, with unimaginable consequences. He has vowed to go, even though raising relief funds is not easy. However, the association will do its best as a matter of benevolence. He will endure long journeys, undeterred by thorns and braving dangers. Director Zhang and the relief workers, at a time when a major disaster awaits relief and the local area is unsettled, are traveling thousands of miles to carry out relief work in Shaanxi. Their enthusiasm and determination are commendable. Hopefully, the disaster victims in Shaanxi and Henan can have their suffering slightly reduced.

Zhabei Businesses Retain Director Ni

Ni Zhecheng, director of the first district of the fourth precinct of the Municipal Police Bureau, received instructions from Director Yuan on the 20th of this month to transfer to the Inspection Department. Upon hearing the news, businesses in Zhabei gathered at the former site of the Zhabei Eleventh Road Business Association at 10:00 AM yesterday to discuss and petition for his retention and reinstatement. Over a hundred businesses from areas like Mongolia Road, Xinjiang Road, Guangfu Road, Manchuria Road, Datong Road, Huasheng Road, Jucheng, Renhe, Tongsheng, and Yifeng attended. Mr. She Guanting, owner of Yifeng Lumber Mill, chaired the meeting. All agreed that Director Ni had served in Zhabei for over a decade, providing meticulous service in maintaining local order and protecting commerce. He has consistently performed well and has been recognized by his superiors and the current Director Yuan as a rare and virtuous police officer. A unanimous decision was made to retain him. A document was drafted, led by Mr. Wang Binyan, a local notable from Zhabei, with all the businesses affixing their seals. The document was submitted to Mayor Zhang of the Municipal Government and Director Yuan of the Public Security Bureau, requesting that they heed the public's plea, revoke the transfer order, and immediately reinstate him as director to satisfy public expectations.

Russian Automobile Accident

▲ Driving Across Boundaries and Hitting a Girl

Zhou, a resident of No. 65 Xiaoyou Lane, Xujiahui, Shanghai, has a daughter named Xingzhen, who is ten years old. Yesterday at 2:10 PM, while returning home after shopping on the street, she was passing in front of Xu Ge Cheng's hat shop on Haig Road at the boundary, when suddenly a French Concession police officer No. 140, Russian Bao Baofu (transliteration), along with his brother and girlfriend, drove his own car (license number 7883) from north to south, entering the Chinese territory road and hitting Zou Xingzhen, knocking her to the ground. The Russian, realizing he had caused an accident, immediately tried to escape. Fortunately, Xie Yongzhang, a police officer from the third post in the area, noticed and pursued him, stopping the car. Unexpectedly, the Russian woman was extremely fierce and tried to assault Officer Xie. As the crowd grew, they voiced their disapproval. Luckily, the Public Security Bureau was nearby. Director Xu, hearing the commotion, realized there was an incident and immediately sent Inspector Xu Tao and Patrol Leader Wang Zhentang with police officers to disperse the crowd and prevent violence. He also advised the Russian to drive the car to the station to prevent further incidents. However, the Russian woman, unable to communicate, arbitrarily cursed and shouted for assistance from the French soldiers stationed there. Fortunately, the French soldiers knew the incident occurred in Chinese territory and ignored her. Patrol Leader Wang, seeing the situation was not good and fearing they would escape to the Concession, pushed the car, along with the three Russians, to the station for detention. He also sent the injured girl to the Aurora Hospital on Rue Père Robert for treatment. It is reported that she suffered serious head, face, and waist injuries, and her life may be in danger. The driver who caused the accident (i.e., police officer Bao Baofu) and the other two Russians were temporarily handed over to French Concession detectives Ge Lai'er for questioning. All losses and violations will be the responsibility of the French Concession.

Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory issued the following weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday: The sky will be mostly cloudy along the coast of the country and in the Yangtze River basin. There will be northeast to southeast winds over the Yellow Sea and the East China Sea. Winds in the Yangtze River basin will be directionless. The weather in the Xisha Islands is poor. To the Editor: Having read your newspaper's April 18th article, "Yanghang Security Corps Drama Fundraiser Causes Trouble," it does not correspond with the facts. Our corps held an entertainment event for five days starting on April 1st to raise funds to purchase firearms. What your newspaper published is likely based on inaccurate rumors. We are specifically requesting a correction to clarify the truth. Respectfully, Baoshan County First District Security Corps, Baoshan County Public Security Bureau Directly Subordinate First Police Precinct, April 19th.
