Free Talk

Laugh It Off

— Hai Ke

▲A: Why did Napoleon say that a pen is mightier than ten thousand Mausers? What power does the pen have after all?

B: Because a pen can sign checks for thousands upon thousands. But you can't use a Mauser rifle to sign a check.

Wife: If someone sits on your hat, what will you do?

Husband: Then I'll scold him as a blockhead, a stupid donkey.

Wife: Blockhead, stupid donkey, don't sit on my hat.

▲A: That Doctor Bing is truly an absent-minded person. He's probably the only one I've ever seen like that in my life.

B: What happened?

A: He got married last week. During the ceremony, the bride held out her hand so that he could put the wedding band on her finger. Instead, he took her pulse and told her to stick out her tongue for him to see.

▲Man: Darling, I'm proposing to you. Why are you crying instead? Did I say something that offended you?

Woman: No, no. (Still crying softly)

Man: Then why are you crying?

Woman: I'm twenty-five years old this year. My mother has been nagging me, saying that I'm inactive and that even the neighbor's yellow dog doesn't want me. Now you want me, so I'm crying with joy.

A Record of Hearing Qin Music at Sea

— Zheng Yimei

Living in a remote area of Songjiang, I feel a sense of emptiness. It is difficult to find one or two kindred spirits to converse with about the past and present to alleviate my poverty. Suddenly, Qian Zihua sent me a letter inviting me to a feast at Jue Lin's place, saying that he had invited several qin music friends, painting companions, and Buddhists for an evening of enjoyment. I was delighted to hear this and went. Zihua had a grand plan to travel south and visit the tomb of Sakyamuni. He described the details in great detail. Later, Mr. Zhang Yuguang, Wang Taomin, Yuan Xilian, Zhao Lanting and others arrived gracefully. We all took our seats. The few vegetarian dishes were delicious. Xilian is a legal scholar, but recently he has been devoted to Zen Buddhism. His conversation was mostly about Buddhist terms, saying that we all have our own karma for entering and leaving the world. The only thing to do is to always keep the Bodhi mind in mind, which is a good thing. This is indeed a famous saying. Zihua took out a fan-shaped booklet with Xun Huisheng's landscape painting and Mei Lanfang's flower paintings. The landscape painting was full of ink charm, and the flower painting was a painting of the Ten Sisters, with beautiful colors, which was especially exquisite. Tao is a famous painter. He talked about the coloring of ancient people. There are light and heavy colors. The lighter ones are delicate, and the heavier ones are calm. Often, the front is colored, and then the back is dyed to set it off. Some are colored and then brushed off, and then reset repeatedly to see its thickness. Modern people do not have this skill. Tao Min also played the qin. According to him, the qin must be more than a hundred years old to be played. Its sound is dull and dull, not as bright as the old one. The paint is easy to crack. The plum blossom crack is the most common, followed by the snake belly crack, and then the ox hair crack. It is a pity that this tune has not been played for a long time. There is a sense of dust on the Zhu string. It should be taken care of slowly. Although he is not willing to live in Boya, he should also ask the scholars to be Zhong Ziqi. Lanting listened to it and suddenly jumped up and said. I have a qin friend, Lin Suyuan, who is from Fujian. He likes to travel. He always carries Jiao Tong with him when he travels north and south. He has come to Shanghai and lives in the Grand China Hotel. The dance floor is next door, and the barbarian music is noisy. However, he closed the door quietly, playing the qin to relieve his boredom, forgetting that he was in the midst of a soft red world. He is a true noble man. Why don't we visit him? After eating, Yuguang and Taomin still had other appointments, so they left in a hurry. We then went to Tibet Road together. Xilian said. There is a saying that playing the qin to a cow. We do not understand the rhythm, is it a cow? We all laughed. When we arrived, Lin Junsuyuan, who was thin and had a beautiful beard, was there. There was a qin on the table, and he was dusting it. After the introduction, I looked at the qin. It was full of ancient charm. It was an old object from the Zhu Ming Dynasty. It was engraved with the inscription. It was made in ancient times and repaired in modern times. It also shows the heart of heaven and earth. I asked him to play it. Jun was humble again and again. He began to play the second part of Gui Qulai. The sound was as fine as the weeping of insects, as far as the winding of water, as rapid as the sudden arrival of summer rain and the sudden wind. Listening intently, all thoughts were eliminated. Therefore, the saying that those who play the qin are forbidden in the past is not false. The sound of the qin stopped, but the remaining sound still lingered between the fingers, making people feel far away. It was already midnight. So I said goodbye and returned. I wrote it down as Hong Zhao.

The Strange Story of a Cat Ringing the Doorbell

— Qian

A few dozen steps from my house is the residence of my classmate Mr. Liu. Mr. Liu has a passion for cats. He keeps more than thirty cats, which consume countless fish. Among them are two tortoiseshell cats, given by his sister. They are the most gentle and pleasing. Mr. and Mrs. Liu love them like the apples of their eyes. Not only do they share their meals and sleep with them, but they also strictly forbid servants from harming a single hair on them. Once, a servant accidentally touched a cat's ear and was scolded by Mr. Liu. This was a laughing matter for a while.

In the twelfth month of last year, one of these tortoiseshell cats, named "Jin Si", suddenly disappeared without a trace. Mr. Liu searched for her everywhere, but to no avail. He was very frustrated. The second tortoiseshell cat, named "Yin Si," lost its partner due to its sister's disappearance, and cried all day long, refusing to eat. Mr. Liu felt even more uneasy when he saw this.

Someone told him a secret method for finding cats, boasting that it was extremely effective. Mr. Liu knew that this was a superstitious act, but out of love for his cat, he tried it anyway. The method involved placing a bowl of water on the stove, filling it with clear water, and placing a weighing pole with a weighing hammer and hook on the mouth of the bowl. There was nothing else different. Mr. Liu did as he was told. After more than a month, there was still no trace of the cat, so he gradually forgot about it.

The other day, late at night, Mr. and Mrs. Liu were sleeping soundly under their quilts when they suddenly heard the doorbell ringing loudly, deafeningly. Mr. Liu was awakened by this and thought that at this late hour, who would be an unwelcome guest? Probably a gang of thieves. He couldn't help but feel a chill down his spine. While he was hesitating, the doorbell rang again, even louder, mixed with the sound of a cat meowing. The sound was very familiar. Mr. Liu got out of bed, put on his clothes, and went to the door to see what was going on. As soon as he opened the door, the bell rang again, but there was no one there. The cold wind was blowing, threatening to extinguish the fire. Mr. Liu saw that there was no one outside the door and almost cried out in alarm.

At this time, the cat's mournful cry was heard intermittently, close at hand. Mr. Liu looked around and caught sight of his lost cat "Jin Si," crouching high on the doorstep, ringing the doorbell with its paw, looking quite comical. Mr. Liu was overjoyed. He held the cat in his arms, closed the door, and returned to his room. He told his wife, "Jin Si is back! Jin Si is back!" His wife was also overjoyed and gave Jin Si a sweet kiss.

The day before yesterday, I ran into Mr. Liu on the road. Mr. Liu happily told me about the cat's recovery. I smiled and said, "Jin Si didn't climb into the house through the roof, but came up with the idea of ringing the doorbell. You don't blame her for disturbing your dreams, but instead find it funny and love her even more. Is she a reincarnation of a raccoon dog?" Mr. Liu nodded and laughed loudly.

Jin Si returned safely, and I also benefited greatly. My house keeps dozens of pigeons, which are coveted by wild cats. Jin Si and her sister Yin Si often come to guard them. Last year, they fought a deadly battle with two wild cats in my garden. Although they suffered minor neck injuries, they finally drove the two cats away, and my pigeons were spared.

A Record of a Large Lantern in the Sky

— Xu Xiaoting

For national day celebrations and revolutionary anniversaries, celebrations are held everywhere, and lantern parades are always held. Lantern parades are usually held at night. The lights are bright and the country is happy. We see them everywhere. However, I have never heard of a lantern parade being held in the sky. I will now record the story of my friend Mr. Zhao Qichang's lantern in the sky to prove my point.

The spring is bright and beautiful, and all things are competing for beauty. In this beautiful sunny weather, children like to play and compete to fly kites. Gongshuzi made Sen Yuan. Rhyme stories are spread. This kind of toy has been popular for thousands of years. My friend Zhao Qichang also loves it. Every year in February and March, he racked his brains to make various shapes of insects, fish, birds and animals and put them in the sky. A few days ago, he had a whimsical idea. He used cellophane to paste dozens of lanterns. Each one was connected by a line. Another dry flashlight was embedded inside. At night, the flashlight was turned on. Dozens of lanterns were carried to the suburbs and released. A gust of wind. They all rose into the wind. At this time, each lantern was a foot away from each other. Outside the cellophane, the electric light was bright. It swayed in the sky and suddenly formed a long snake formation. At first glance, it was walking heel to toe. It was no different from the lantern parade on the ground. The order was well maintained and perhaps even exceeded it. This is truly a new way to play in the kite craze with a whimsical idea. Those who have a kite addiction, why not imitate it?

A Record of a Westerner's Estate Analysis

— Jie Lu

The owner of a certain foreign firm at sea is an Englishman. More than fifty years ago, he came to Shanghai alone and operated real estate with a small amount of capital. After decades of hard work, he accumulated three to four million yuan. Although he is not as rich as Hardoon, his keen vision and successful operation can be compared with Hardoon. After the Opium War, Chinese and foreign trade was carried out. The foreign concession was only ten miles long. There was no such prosperity as today. The owner was good at planning and multiplying wealth. He bought cheap, barren land. After managing it, it is now a prosperous area on the sea. The value per mu is hundreds of thousands of gold. It is appropriate for a fat-faced man to be a wealthy man. However, the owner has a strange hobby. He owns extremely large real estate at sea, but he rents a few rooms to live in. He does not travel by car. Sometimes he walks as a car. He is happy. Alas, people at sea drive motorcycles and fly around, as if everyone is rich. In fact, as the ancients said, "The car is dazzling and the people are exhausted." They are everywhere. Compared with the owner, how can they not be ashamed to death? However, the owner is so frugal, could it be that he has become a money-grubber? But it is not. The owner knows that he is old, so he made a will. Half of his fortune will be used to help the education business. The Chinese who have served in his foreign firm for a long time will also receive tens of thousands of gold. It can be said to be generous. Alas, the poison of inheritance is the deepest among Chinese people. Today, there are many brothers and sisters who file lawsuits over inheritance disputes. Isn't it the evil of the inheritance system? How can we take a certain Westerner as a model? Alas, it can be customized.

Travel Notes in Southeast Asia (15)

— Linghua

I arrived in Singapore on the morning of the 20th. But it is not easy to get to Singapore. There are two conditions. One is to check the passport. The second is to check the epidemic. This is the iron law at all docks. It is not easy to get to Singapore. The English are more liberal in checking passports than the French. The British colony has been able to succeed at sea because it has a reputation for generosity and freedom. The English just check and stamp it. The French spend a lot of time writing a lot of documents, which is just a description of their narrowness and harshness. In addition, the doctor who checks the disease has great power. There is only one small boat that comes to check the epidemic. A yellow flag is hung on the epidemic checking boat. If this flag does not fall, merchant ships are not allowed to enter the port. You must watch this flag fall before passenger ships are allowed to enter the port freely. I can't help but admit that Westerners often use hygiene as an excuse. It seems that they value life very much. Why can they mobilize 20 million people in Europe to kill each other within ten days? How cheap is their life? It is really upside down. What we should know here is that the French postal ship is very clean. We only saw the epidemic checking boat come, but we did not see it checking the guests for the epidemic. If the British ship is in the fourth class or below, it is said that they must take off their clothes and check their bodies. Those who have the epidemic cannot land. There is another small island. They are placed there. Their clothes are fumigated with sulfur. They must collect firewood and cook rice themselves. After going through 1727, they can enter the port after they recover from the disease. I often tell people that there are many difficult things in the world to understand, such as the Thorough Principle written by Lu Xinjun. Today, Europe and the United States are politics of the rich, so poverty is a crime. The bodies of the poor are the homes of epidemic insects. In fact, the bodies of the poor are healthier than those of the rich. For example, tuberculosis is more common among the rich. If we are involved in Russia, it is the opposite. They are politics of the poor. The rich are a crime. The sun is near and Chang'an is far away. How can we determine what is right and wrong? However, if we use the Chinese culture of neutrality to measure it fairly, it is not fair. Sin is sin and should not be judged based on wealth. Alas, I am indignant about this, so I am determined to use the new Eastern culture to save the world. Can people of far-sightedness in the world help me?

When I arrived at the dock, there was a hotel in Southeast Asia to pick up guests. They called a car and took my luggage directly to the hotel. They are very skilled at picking up guests. They speak all kinds of dialects. There were Indians at the dock asking for money. They did not give them a penny. They were not checked either. They drove straight to the hotel. The total cost was three yuan and two corners. If you negotiate with the people at the dock yourself, it will cost a lot of money.

I stayed in a room for three yuan a day. The food was not included. It was spacious and clean. Three yuan here is equal to five yuan in Shanghai.

In the afternoon, I visited Chen Lizhi of the Buddhist Association. Wang Zhi'an told me that Wang had died a month ago. He was an important figure in Buddhism. I had received a letter from him. It was very sincere. Now he is dead. Chen took me to visit the Abbot of Tianfu Palace, Zhuan Dao, and stayed at the temple.

On the morning of the 21st, Dao Master asked Chen to take me to the Longshan Temple Garden Building. Chen paid for the accommodation. The people of the Buddhist Association here complained that I did not call earlier so that they could prepare to welcome me.

Warmth in My Heart (176)

— Bao Tianxiao

Chapter 10: Red Flames Rise to the Sky, the Brothel Reveres Filial Piety; At the Banquet, Meeting the Famous Courtesan Hong Nu Shutie

After this fire, Wen Guizhi had no place to live. She had to stay in a hotel nearby. At that time, one person told ten people, and ten people told a hundred people. People in the brothel, especially, liked to talk about right and wrong. Everyone said that Wen Guizhi was really a filial grandson. If it weren't for her, this old lady would have gone with the Fire God Bodhisattva. That Lord Yan knew about this and came to see her the next day. It just so happened that this day, a friend invited him to drink wine with courtesans. He called Wen Guizhi to the stage. Everyone surrounded her and asked about the fire yesterday. Many courtesans in the brothel used Wen Guizhi's desperate attempt to save her grandmother from the fire as a topic of conversation. That Lord Yan was also a literary figure. Many of his friends were not only dignitaries, but also literati. Some people even wrote poems to praise Wen Guizhi. Once praised, her reputation increased tenfold. Many friends urged Lord Yan, saying that you have such a good person, not only is her appearance good, but her temperament and morality are also so top-notch. Why haven't you hidden her in a golden house? Isn't this a missed opportunity? Lord Yan originally liked Wen Guizhi very much. Every time he called for her to sing, he would call for her. Sometimes when he was happy, he would call for her three or four times a day. If she was a little late, he would stretch his neck and look for her. Now, he couldn't stand the praise from everyone. And she, in fact, had such an anecdote that was enough to make people amazed and praised. There was no happier thing in the world than to have one's lover praised by others. So today, Lord Yan's face was radiant. He opened his mouth wide and just laughed, like a wooden fish that had been knocked open. But he asked Wen Guizhi, "Then have all your things been burned? Your loss this time is not small." Wen Guizhi also honestly said, "I don't have many jewelry to begin with. Fortunately, I wore them all on my body when I went to your brothel yesterday. Lord Yan, you also know my temper. I don't like to wear them when I rent them at a high price. But the clothes, regardless of leather, cotton, or single, have all been burned, because those clothes boxes were all piled up in my grandmother's room." Lord Yan immediately wanted to comfort her, "Clothes are limited after all. Don't take it to heart. I will compensate you for how many clothes were burned." Everyone present clapped their hands in agreement, saying, "That's right, that's right. Lord Yan should compensate immediately. Burn the old ones and let Lord Yan make new ones. It's not just compensation, but it should also be a reward." Another friend joked, "This is all because you two are too enthusiastic. Because you're too hot, you caused this fire."

Yarn and Cotton: Stalemated Yarn Market

The yarn market was sluggish and uninteresting. Both bulls and bears were manufacturers with strong capabilities and fierce competition. Overall, the unstable situation, stagnant spot sales, and relatively thick inventories made the general trend soften. Outsiders were hesitant to take action given this situation, resulting in small fluctuations. New deliveries were scarce, and long-term trading was minimal, with many short selling orders. However, the situation for this month was still serious. Rumors spread that sellers had taken delivery of about 2,000-3,000 bales of 20-count Five Blessings and Shepherd yarns. This news weakened market sentiment and caused a decline.

▲ Mixed Trends in Yarn Futures In the morning session, the bull side held firm, and rumors of labor unrest led some retail investors to buy in. Near-term contracts rose by 0.6-0.7 yuan. News that the labor unrest was untrue caused a sudden drop in the market. At the same time, the Osaka Sampin Exchange (Sanshin) telegraph also reported a small decline, loosening the market. As a result, the current month contract fell by 0.03 yuan, while long-term contracts rose by 0.013 yuan. In the afternoon, sellers prepared to deliver, further weakening the market. Soybean Futures Weak, Spot Prices Stable

Yesterday, near-term continuous soybeans were weak. Although the telegraph from Dalian was flat, the current month weakened due to buyers gradually selling to close positions. As for sellers, they were preparing to deliver due to weak spot sales. As a result, the standard price returned to 5 taels, 3 qian, and 7 fen, a decrease of 0.03-0.04 yuan. Spot soybean prices remained stable, with high-grade soybeans at around 0.04 yuan and medium-grade soybeans at 0.036-0.037 yuan. Sales were mainly for local small-scale mills. Traders from inland regions were observing due to low profitability. The soybean market was currently stagnant.

High Rice Futures Prices, Stagnant Sales

Yesterday's foreign rice market turned from rising to stable. After the sharp rise of 0.1 yuan and more in the afternoon of the previous day, various trading groups stopped buying, leading to extreme sluggishness yesterday morning. However, after a small price drop, the Wenzhou trading group, local traders, and low-priced outlets began to open the market, with a total of over 20,000. This allowed the market to stabilize. No. 1 Saigon was offered at 15.9 yuan, No. 2 at 15 yuan, small broken rice at 15.2 yuan, and big broken Min Dang rice at 15.1 yuan, a slight decrease of 0.1 yuan compared to the highest price of the previous day. Overseas rice futures prices were reported to be rising, and foreign firms were adhering to their positions. The prices for returned goods were very high, but due to concerns about market disruption, most were observing and not selling. Therefore, overall market transactions were very limited.

Sunny Weather Causes Flour Market to Fall

Yesterday, the prices for all months of flour fell across the board. Due to the gradually improving weather in recent days, people had expected higher prices. However, traders from inland regions reported that wheat seedlings were growing very well, as the climate was suitable for wheat development. If this situation did not change drastically, a good harvest could be expected in the future, causing market sentiment to soften. Subsequently, traders from Tianjin sold some near-term and long-term contracts, believing that the prices were too high given the arrival of new flour. Therefore, they sold as market sentiment weakened. This was the observation of spot sales groups. It is unknown whether traders from inland regions were moved by this. As a result, the price for this month fell by 0.005 yuan compared to the previous week, May fell by 0.0125 yuan, June fell by 0.015 yuan, July fell by 0.0125 yuan, August fell by 0.01 yuan, and September fell by 0.005 yuan.

Wheat Futures: Near-Term Decline, Long-Term Stability

Yesterday, the futures market for wheat showed a near-term decline and long-term stability. The current month saw declines due to bulls selling, while factories remained unmoved. In addition, as the delivery date approached, speculative long positions took the opportunity to close out. As for inventories, the arrival of new supplies was not as strong as expected due to the time of year when new crops were emerging. Speculators dared not hoard goods. This was the biggest reason for the decline. Due to the excellent weather, wheat seedlings were reported to be growing well, causing market sentiment to soften slightly in June. In July, August, and September, some traders from Wuxi sold some contracts, while others continued to buy, resulting in a state of mutual rejection. If the weather remains unchanged, the market may gradually weaken. As a result, the price for this month fell by 0.04 yuan compared to the previous week, June fell by 0.02 yuan, July fell by 0.01 yuan, August rose by 0.01 yuan, and September remained unchanged. In the spot wheat market, high-grade wheat prices remained stable due to strong factory demand, while medium-grade wheat prices were low and weak. Qingjiangpu, Suzhou, Xuzhou, and Bengbu wheat were offered at 5 taels and 1 qian; Shashi wheat was offered at 4 taels and 7.5 qian, with a total of 18,000 bags. Fuxin handled 14,000 bags, and Fufeng handled 4,000 bags.

Silk and Tea: Foreign Firms Closed for Holiday, No Market for Silk

▲ Regular Business to Resume Today

Yesterday, local foreign firms observed a holiday for Christmas, customs were closed, and there was no market for foreign exchange. The silk market remained closed. Today (the 22nd), foreign firms will resume business, and the silk market will return to normal.

Recent News on Anhui and Jiangxi Tea

▲ Qimen Black Tea Gardens Have Opened The weather has warmed up in the past ten days, with frequent rainfall, causing the tea buds to develop rapidly. The earliest gardens can be opened recently. Local farmers are concerned that the tea will grow too quickly and that they will not be able to pick and process it in time. Fortunately, the weather turned cold yesterday, slowing down the growth of the tea leaves and preventing them from becoming too mature. Currently, Wufuqi tea firms in Jingzhen are purchasing rice, but the city has banned its export, preventing its shipment. This has caused the firms to be stranded in Jingzhen and extremely anxious. They are urgently requesting that the city's Party Committee and the Fuliang County government provide assistance, as the tea picking and processing season is approaching and cannot be delayed. It is reported that the county government has agreed to find a solution, and as soon as permission to transport is granted, they will be able to enter the mountains and start production.

▲ Anren Tea Expected to Open for Sale Soon Anren is an important tea-producing area in Jiangxi Province, with a production volume comparable to Yushan and Dexing. The tea leaves in this area sprout after the spring and summer harvests, and can be picked and sold three or four times until the fall. Tea firms from Dexing, Hekou, Yushan, and Yangzhuang often send personnel to Anren to purchase tea. In recent years, due to poor export sales, the sales of Yangzhuang firms have decreased. Although domestic stores and firms still have strong demand, the low selling price has not benefited the farmers much. This year, the tea leaves in this area have developed quite early. Farmers are rushing to pick and process the tender buds. A few gardens have already opened. Tea stores and vendors from this province have been sending their employees to the mountains to search for and buy tea. It is expected that sales will begin in about a week. (13th)

Piece Goods: Active Procurement in the Street

▲ Over 200 Pieces of Eastern Goods Sold Yesterday

▲ Hangzhou to Collect Special Tax in Advance, Accelerating Shipments

The past few days have been Western holidays, and most firms have stopped business, resulting in a very dull piece goods market. Although firms resumed business yesterday, banks remained closed, so only goods in stock at local warehouses could be shipped. Transactions involving bank transfers were still suspended. On the customer sales side, activity was slightly higher due to the lack of arrivals in recent days. Slightly more members of the Cotton Cloth Association arrived yesterday. Over 200 pieces of eastern goods were sold in the street, most of which were transported to Hangzhou due to the upcoming special tax in that area. As a result, shipments were accelerated. Printed linen yarn was shipped in large quantities, with San Ma Tou (brand) at 2 qian, 2 fen, and 7.5 li, Xiang Meiren (brand) at 2 qian and 2.5 fen, and Yang Guifei (brand) at 2 qian and 1.5 fen. Raw foreign yarn continued to fall. Dian Qiuxiang (brand) opened at 8 taels and 3.5 qian, and Tang Taizong (brand) at 8 taels and 2.5 qian, and they were slightly easier to sell. Redyed goods from local factories sold for around 6 taels. Blue-striped serge sold quite well, with Zijinshan (brand) at 1 qian and 6.5 fen, Ersunfu (brand) at 1 qian, 6 fen, and 2.5 li, and Xiaojie Tu (brand) at 1 qian, 7 fen, and 2.5 li. Over 100 pieces were sold, mostly purchased by local traders. However, customers from other regions were still lifeless. There were no additional purchases from the Yangtze River region, except for a few replenishments from Ningbo traders.

Business News

The company is well-organized and specializes in collecting difficult debts for all businesses. The fees are lower than those charged by debt collection agencies established by foreigners. There are two types of contracts: annual and temporary. If litigation is involved, the company will also fully bear the lawyer's fees, litigation fees, and all other fees, in order to demonstrate its commitment to protecting the interests of merchants. Shanghai's commerce is thriving, and there are many debts. Since the company's opening, there has been a surge in the number of people entrusting it with business.

▲ Rongchangxiang of Nanjing Road announced that it is holding a one-month price reduction to benefit Western suit customers. The store anticipated the sharp rise in gold prices last year and purchased a large batch of woolens and ordered a large quantity of new goods from well-known foreign woolen mills. Therefore, its cost is 70-80% cheaper than current market prices. Due to the store's large inventory and low purchase prices, it is taking this opportunity to hold a special three-week sale. Yesterday was the first day of the store's price reduction, and customers were extremely crowded. The most popular items were the French wool suits for 26 yuan and the fancy wool suits for 32 yuan. Other items, such as woolen hats and miscellaneous items, were discounted by 20-10%.

The purpose was to organize young women to study the responsibilities of motherhood, not only to know the way to health, but also to know how to raise children in the future, which is contrary to the Chinese Eastern Ethics of "no one learns to raise children before marrying." Dr. Booker Joseph of the United States, with 20 years of experience, wrote the book "Early Motherhood Group," which, in addition to various methods for organizing the group, details the three major questions of why, how, and what should be the responsibilities of raising children. The book has been translated into Chinese by Ms. Li Guanfang and published by the association. The price is only 0.15 yuan.

The Whispers in the Park · Shi Duo

After lunch, I hurried out of my residence and headed towards Jess Field Park. On the way, I was contemplating how to spend this intoxicating spring afternoon. I planned to take a stroll around the park first, then find a quiet corner, sit down quietly surrounded by greenery, and carefully read a rainbow-colored shield. If I felt like it, I wouldn't even go back for dinner, but wait there for the moon to rise, so that I could reminisce about the unbearable past in the serene night air. Thinking of this, a feeling of ease passed through my chest, and even my breathing seemed smoother.

Arriving at the park gate, I was met by a park guard. Instinctively, I reached into my pocket, preparing to take out my Season Ticket for him to inspect. But after searching all over, I still couldn't find it. Only then did I remember that my ticket was in another coat pocket and I hadn't brought it. Embarrassed, my face flushed repeatedly. I had no choice but to take out twenty cents and walk back to the ticket booth. "What bad luck, wasting this money," I thought to myself as I received the ticket.

As soon as I entered the park gate, a cluster of trees in front of me created a kind of pressure on my mind. When I walked beneath them, I stood there sadly for a long time, looking left and right, as if this place was unfamiliar to me. But that wasn't the case. As I stood there, a unique feeling suddenly came over me. I felt that every leaf and tree here was very lovely. And the birds jumping on the branches, leaking a delicate song from the leaves, made me even more intoxicated. After a long while, I reluctantly walked past.

Suddenly, I emerged from a corner of the park and walked to a unique stone bridge in the park. I saw a group of people leaning on the bridge railing, intently looking down below. Everyone's eyes were focused on a somersaulting mouse, and laughter and the sound of gongs mingled together. I casually walked past, taking about a dozen steps forward, and the lively scene in the center of the park unfolded before my eyes. Small, old, tall, short, red, and green, people crisscrossed, forming a picture of a thriving spring. At that moment, I felt that this park was different. The situation of loneliness and tranquility that had been locked up in the past could only be found in memory now. Thinking this, I walked to a pool of lake water in the middle of the park. At this time, seven or eight foreign children were standing by the lake, exposing their knees, with their sleeves rolled up high, playing with their small sailboats. Groups of people were also crowding on the shore, as if their purpose in coming here was to watch this show.

From there, I went back into the corner of the park. Under the protection of the greenery, I walked slowly, step by step. The spring breeze blew gently, dispelling the stuffiness from my body. I felt a little happy and wanted to find a comfortable seat nearby to sit down quietly and read. However, looking around, all the seats had been occupied by those who were quick on their feet. Disappointed, I had no choice but to continue walking forward. After walking a dozen steps, I could faintly see several cars parked outside the park through the gaps in the greenery. At the same time, the sound of car horns was constantly coming one after another. It turned out that the main gate on the east side was ahead. At this time, tourists poured in from the main gate like a tide, each one bracing themselves and walking quickly into the park.

I stood under a tree, staring blankly. Suddenly, my heart darkened. This group of leisurely people only gave me a suffocating sadness. I felt the gray side of life, and I also felt the glorious corner of life. Ah, life, the cursed urban life. I sighed deeply and turned to walk west. Suddenly, I felt a ray of light coming towards me. It turned out that a fiery sun was already hanging high in the treetops to the west, dyeing everything in the park crimson red.

After running around in the park for a while, I still couldn't get rid of a kind of inexplicable accumulated depression. The lovers holding hands, the charming soft laughter, the simple and noisy commotion—all of these made me resentful. Finally, I walked to a grove of trees in the corner of the park and sat down, intending to rest quietly from then on. However, after sitting for only a few seconds, the buzzing sound that filled the entire space drove me out of the park.

The Mysterious Eastern Island · Liang Xiong Wan

Twelve scientists from the University of Pennsylvania in the United States will depart next spring for Eastern Island, one of the most mysterious places in the South Pacific. This trip may be able to provide a satisfactory solution to the mysteries that scientists have considered inexplicable on this desolate island for two hundred years.

The area of ​​this desolate island is very small, so there are not many indigenous people living there. Along the winding shore are countless tombstones, relics of a long-forgotten people. No one now knows what kind of people built these tombstones, or what era they were built in.

Eastern Island is a triangular volcanic area with an area of ​​only forty-five square miles. Its neighboring islands (approximately two thousand miles from the Chilean coast and one thousand miles west of Eastern Island) are desolate and remote places on earth, uninhabited by anyone.

Eastern Island is very remote from transportation routes, so in 1922, a Spanish exploration ship failed to find it. In the same year, after an earthquake occurred on the island, it took several months to correct the shipowner's report—the island of the dead was lost. Only a few explorers have been there. What they found there is one of the most interesting and unresolved mysteries in the world.

The most interesting thing is the magnificent ancient tombs, of which there are two hundred and sixty, some of which are three hundred feet long and fifteen feet high, with an altar one hundred feet wide in front for people to worship their ancestors. There are more than six hundred tall half-body stone statues on the island. No one has yet found out who carved these stone statues from volcanic rock, or why they carved them like this.

The location of these solemn-faced stone statues (the largest of which are thirty feet high and weigh forty to two hundred and fifty tons) is not fixed. It is said that these many stone statues were used as decorations for tombs, with oval stone slabs lining the tombs. A fisherman who had been there one hundred and fifty years ago saw countless stone idols standing along the shore, facing away from the sea. He was surprised and felt a lot of interest in these things.

These strange-shaped stone corners are generally more than two thousand to five thousand years old. It is possible that their age could be even higher. Are they idols, images of gods for people to pray to, or images of ancient heroes, or images of ancestors? There are no satisfactory answers to these questions.

There are three volcanic craters on the island. The rocks next to the volcanic craters are the raw materials used by the long-forgotten people to carve stone idols. Next to the Lara Ku volcanic crater, there are still many unfinished stone idols placed there. But we are a little skeptical here. In ancient times or the Middle Ages, when machines had not been invented, how did the stonemasons move the completed stone idols from the volcanic crater to the foot of the mountain? This is what we do not understand. Now, many heavy tools have been found on the mountainside and next to the volcanic crater. This is obviously the remains of the workers hundreds of years ago. Moreover, most of the stone statues next to the volcanic crater have not been completed. This can further show that the work at that time must have been stopped by some kind of magic.

Was this demon war, plague, famine, or a special natural disaster that wiped out all these workers? No one knows these things. Although there are many speculations, some people say that this was caused by earthquakes and volcanic eruptions, but he cannot provide geographical evidence to confirm his statement. If an earthquake were to really occur and a volcano were to really erupt, the stone statues and altars and other relics would have long been reduced to pieces, or if they were not broken, they would have been covered by volcanic lava.

In order to break the various mysteries of Eastern Island, the University of Pennsylvania's expedition this time will take a long time to prepare everything. A specially made motor ship worth US$1.5 million will be completed in the near future for this expedition. The ship has been named "Caroline" and is two hundred and fifty feet long. It was donated by Earl Dyer Johnson, a trustee of the University of Pennsylvania and manager of the Victoria Phonograph Company. He will depart for Eastern Island on the same ship as the expedition team.

The most important mission of this expedition is to solve the origin of the Eastern Island natives. Where did these island people come from? How did they get to this remote island? Did they migrate here from "Chile" in South America or "

[Note: There is a break in the text here with partially visible Chinese characters which cannot be translated.]

"Secret"? Or did they live on Amo Island?

There are currently two hundred native Hawaiians living on the island. They do not understand much about the mysterious cemetery of their ancestors, nor do they care about it. They may be the descendants of the original inhabitants of this island, but we cannot say that for sure, because they do not have traditional culture for us to refer to. This expedition will definitely make many contributions to us. Please wait and see with your eyes wide open.

Mr. Nakagawa Kigen Oil Painting Exhibition

Japanese famous painter Mr. Nakagawa Kigen visited China last month to travel and sketch. It is recently heard that he is scheduled to display his recent works at the Penglu Japanese Club on the 26th and 27th of this month for general appreciation. Mr. Nakagawa is a member of the Nikakai. He traveled to Europe several years ago to study art. He has served as a teacher in the Department of Fine Arts of the Bunka Gakuin and a teacher in the Nikakai Painting School in Tokyo. His creation is novel, his painting method is unique and simple, and his brushwork is strong, profound, and full of oriental characteristics. Many newcomers in the country's painting world are influenced by his style, and even the Chinese painting world knows his name. The works to be exhibited this time include more than sixty oil paintings, including landscapes sketched during his trip to China, as well as still life paintings and figure paintings. The exhibition dates are only two days, and there is no admission ticket required for anyone to visit.
